The Imam's Pause: A Reversal of Roles (Qalb al-Mawdu')
Definition and ruling on imam's pause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers the imam's pause for the follower's recitation as makruh tahrimi using the concept of qalb al-mawdu'.

Core Idea
The imam must lead, not wait: pausing for the follower's recitation reverses the prayer's order.

In congregational prayer, the imam's role is to be followed. Some schools suggest the imam pause after al-Fatiha so followers can recite. The Hanafi school, however, views this as a reversal of roles (qalb al-mawdu'). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi ruling, examining the hadith evidence and the logical argument that such a pause disrupts the imam-follower relationship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Recognize the specific act in question: the imam pausing after reciting al-Fatiha to allow the follower to recite their own al-Fatiha.
2
Define Qalb al-Mawdu'
Understand the term qalb al-mawdu' (reversal of roles). In Hanafi fiqh, it refers to violating the proper order of the imam-follower relationship.
3
Apply to the Scenario
Explain why pausing for the follower's recitation constitutes qalb al-mawdu': the imam becomes a follower by waiting, inverting his role.
The imam's role is to lead, not to wait.
4
Examine the Hadith Evidence
Analyze the hadith of Ubadah: the Prophet did not pause for the follower's recitation; his pauses were for other reasons.
5
Contrast with Shafi'i View
Compare the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i view, noting the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

And the imam's pause so that the follower recites: reversal of the subject. And the hadith of Ubadah testifies to the permissibility of reciting al-Fatiha in silent prayers and also in audible prayers during the pause: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed Fajr and the recitation became heavy on him...' [1] His saying: 'The imam's pause...' etc. — to rebut a potential objection. The objector's argument: that it is permissible for the imam to pause between his recitation so that the beginner recites, as is customary among the Shafi'i imams, who pause after al-Fatiha for the follower to recite al-Fatiha, then begin the surah. In that case, if the follower recites, he is not violating the verse, nor the hadith of contention, nor the hadith of listening, etc. The rebuttal: the imam's role (mawdu') is that the follower follows him and imitates him, just as the follower's role is to follow his imam in his actions. So if the imam pauses for the purpose of the follower's recitation, it results in the imam becoming a follower of the follower — this is reversal of the subject. From another angle, the imam's role — i.e., what is established and decreed for him legally in the standing state — is recitation. If he pauses, that violates his role. It is objected to this: that violation of the role only results if his role were only recitation, and pausing for the follower to recite is not a reversal of the subject. The analogy is what the jurists mentioned: that the imam should glorify Allah in bowing and prostration so that followers can complete their remembrances; they also said: if the imam knows that reciting the supplications after the tashahhud is burdensome for the follower, he leaves them. Indeed, the discussion is about the proof of this customary pause among the Shafi'is. What is established from reports is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pause in the first rak'ah a long pause before recitation in which he said praises and turning to Allah and other supplications, and he used to pause a brief pause after 'Wala al-dallin' and also after finishing recitation to catch his breath. But it is not authentically and clearly established that he paused so that the follower could recite.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling concerning the imam's pause for the follower's recitation, analyzing whether it constitutes a reversal of roles (qalb al-mawdu'). The commentator begins by stating the rule: 'The imam's pause so that the follower recites: reversal of the subject.' Then he provides the hadith of Ubadah as evidence for permissibility of reciting al-Fatiha during pauses, but this hadith is actually a continuation from the previous section. The core discussion rebuts a potential objection from those who argue that the imam may pause for the follower to recite, as the Shafi'is do. The rebuttal explains that the imam's fundamental role (mawdu') is to be followed, not to become a follower himself. Pausing for the follower's recitation reverses this relationship. However, the commentator acknowledges an objection: the imam's role is not only recitation; pausing for a valid purpose (like allowing the follower to complete their duty) does not necessarily reverse the roles, as seen in other cases like the imam pausing for supplications. The commentator then questions whether such a pause is authentically established from the Prophet's practice. He notes that the Prophet did pause for other reasons (like saying opening supplications or catching his breath), but not specifically for the follower to recite. Thus, the Hanafi position is that the imam should not pause for the follower's recitation; such a pause would alter the established order of prayer.

Key Terms
قلب الموضوع (qalb al-mawdu'): A reversal of roles: the imam (who should be followed) becomes a follower by pausing for the follower's recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis consider it problematic for the imam to pause specifically so that the follower can recite al-Fatiha?
A) Because the follower should not recite at all.
B) Because it reverses the imam's role from leader to follower.
C) Because the imam's recitation is more important.
D) Because the prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
The imam should not pause for the follower's recitation; doing so reverses the intended roles and is makruh tahrimi.

Follower's Responses in Prayer: The Ruling on Silence and the Exception
Commentary expanding the ruling on the follower's silence during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a follower's response during prayer to the imam's recitation of verses or sermon, and identify the single exception where quiet response is permitted by istihsan.

Core Idea
In obligatory prayer, the follower must remain silent; the Prophet's example was for voluntary prayer, except when the imam recites a verse commanding salawat.

When the imam recites verses of encouragement or warning, or delivers a sermon, or sends blessings, the follower's instinct may be to respond appropriately. However, the Hanafi school teaches that listening takes precedence over responding in obligatory prayer, based on the command to be silent. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the one exception allowed by juristic preference (istihsan).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a follower (muqtadi) hearing the imam recite a verse of targhib or tarhib, or delivering a sermon, or sending blessings. The general ruling: the follower must remain silent and not respond verbally.
This applies during obligatory prayers (fard).
2
Locate the primary evidence
The hadith of Hudhayfah shows the Prophet responding to verses, but Hanafi scholars restrict its application to voluntary prayer (nafl) because the follower is obligated to listen to the imam.
The hadith is narrated in Sahih Muslim and Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra.
3
Understand the exception via istihsan
The exception: when the imam recites a verse that commands sending blessings on the Prophet (e.g., 33:56), the follower may quietly send salawat. This is by istihsan, not obligation.
Istiḥsān (juristic preference) allows a relaxation of the general prohibition to combine the virtues of listening and responding.
4
Note the underlying principle
The obligation to listen (wajib) overrides general permissibility of supplication during prayer. Listening protects the integrity of the congregation and the sermon.
If listening is compromised, the prayer may become makruh.

This detail is in the commentary on the imam's speech and its annotations, and in 'As-Sa‘āyah'. [1] His statement: 'verse of encouragement' — like verses indicating glad tidings to believers of Paradise, or 'warning' i.e., intimidation: like verses indicating threat. So the follower does not ask for Paradise at that time, nor seek refuge from Hellfire, nor does he glorify at verses of glorification, nor send blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ upon hearing his name, but rather listens and remains silent, due to the general nature of verses and hadiths that indicate silence. (2) And what Muslim and others narrated from Hudhayfah: that the Prophet ﷺ, when he came across a verse of glorification, he would glorify; when he came across a request, he would ask; and when he came across a seeking of refuge, he would seek refuge. Our companions interpreted it as applying to voluntary prayer, and permitted it for the one praying alone and for the imam in voluntary prayer if he is secure from burdening the followers, as stated in 'Al-‘Ināyah', 'Al-Bināyah', 'Fatḥ al-Qadīr', and others. [2] His statement: 'or delivers a sermon' — coordinated with his statement 'his imam recites' — meaning he does not recite anything but listens and remains silent, even if his imam delivers the sermon. And in it is an indication that it is preferable for the sermon-giver on Friday and the two ‘Īds to be the imam, and if someone else delivers, it is permissible, as in 'An-Nihāyah'. And it is possible that the meaning is 'or the sermon-giver delivers', due to hadiths indicating the obligation of silence for the listener of the sermon and prohibition of engaging in anything that disrupts the sermon. [3] His statement: 'or sends blessings' — the pronoun refers to the sermon-giver; i.e., when the sermon-giver sends blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ in the sermon, the listener does not occupy himself with sending blessings, so as not to disrupt listening. [4] His statement: 'except if he recites' — an exception from his statement 'or sends blessings'; meaning the listener does not recite anything, even if the sermon-giver sends blessings, except when he recites a verse that contains the command to send blessings; then the listener quietly sends blessings upon the Prophet. (1) This is by way of istiḥsān, not obligation; because in it is obtaining both virtues. The correct view is that there is no prohibition of all that they forbade during the pauses, as long as it does not disrupt listening, without restricting to a particular time, as we clarified in 'As-Sa‘āyah'.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is from the sharḥ (commentary) on Al-Wiqāyah, discussing the ruling of the follower (muqtadī) during the prayer when the imam recites certain types of verses or performs certain actions. The author first states the general ruling: if the imam recites a verse of encouragement (targhīb) or warning (tarhīb), or delivers a sermon (khuṭbah), or sends blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ (ṣalāt), the follower should not respond verbally—neither by asking for Paradise, seeking refuge, glorifying, nor sending blessings. Instead, he must listen attentively, based on Quranic verses and hadiths that command silence during prayer and sermons. The hadith from Hudhayfah is cited, which shows that the Prophet ﷺ would respond appropriately during his recitation, but the Hanafi scholars interpret this as specific to voluntary prayer (nafl), because the follower in obligatory prayer is bound to listen to the imam. The commentator then addresses each scenario: for the khuṭbah, the follower should listen even if the khuṭbah is given by someone other than the imam; for sending blessings, the follower should not respond because it would distract from listening. An exception is made when the imam recites a verse that commands sending blessings (like Sūrat al-Aḥzāb, 33:56); in that case, the follower may quietly respond with ṣalawāt, but this is recommended (istiḥsān), not obligatory. The reasoning is that this preserves both the virtue of listening and the virtue of responding. The author notes that there is no harm in allowing such responses during pauses as long as listening is not compromised.

Key Terms
ترغيب (targhīb): A verse that encourages towards Paradise and good deeds.
ترهيب (tarhīb): A verse that warns against Hellfire and sin.
خطب (khaṭaba): The imam delivers the Friday or ‘Īd sermon.
صلى على النبي (ṣallā ‘alā an-nabī): The imam sends blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ.
استحسان (istiḥsān): A juristic preference that leads to a relaxation of the general prohibition in this case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) When the imam recites a verse that commands sending blessings upon the Prophet (e.g., ayat al-salawat).
D) When the imam recites the name of the Prophet ﷺ.

Key Takeaway
The follower in obligatory prayer must listen silently; the only exception by istihsan is when the imam recites a verse commanding salat, then quiet response is permitted.

The Hanafi Ruling on Sending Salutations During Prayer: Istihsan Over Obligation
Commentary on ruling of reciting salat upon Prophet during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on reciting salat upon the Prophet during prayer and explain why it is based on istihsan rather than wujub.

Core Idea
Sending salutations during prayer is mustahabb by istihsan, not wajib — preferring two virtues without disturbance.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies a common point of discussion: whether one must send salutations upon the Prophet (ṣallallāhu 'alayhi wa sallam) during the prayer. The ruling is not obligatory but recommended, derived through istihsan (juristic preference). Let's examine the reasoning and the conditions that make this permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting ṣalāt (salutations) upon the Prophet during the ritual prayer. The author states it is ‘alā sabīl al-istiḥsān lā ‘alā sabīl al-wujūb — based on istihsan, not obligation. So the ruling is mustahabb (recommended).
‘Ṣalāt’ here means the du'ā' for the Prophet, not the prayer itself.
2
Understand the basis: istihsan
Istihsan is a Hanafi source of law that allows preferring a ruling that seems more fitting over strict analogy or an apparent evidence. The commentator reasons: reciting salutations during prayer allows one to attain two virtues — the virtue of sending salutations and the virtue of maintaining the proper silence of the prayer. This is judged as praiseworthy, hence mustahabb.
Istihsan is rejected by Shāfi'īs, leading to a difference of opinion.
3
Examine the condition: silent pauses
The permissibility is restricted to the silent pauses (sakatāt) in the prayer — moments when the imam is silent (e.g., after the Fatiha, between takbirs). The condition is that it does not impair listening to the imam's recitation. There is no restriction to a specific pause; any silent moment suffices.
If one recites aloud or during imam's recitation, it may become makruh.
4
Note the cross-madhhab disagreement
The author acknowledges that some scholars consider it wājib (obligatory). The Hanafīs choose the view of mustahabb because the evidence (dalīl) for obligation is not qat'ī (definitive). The underlying basis is istihsan, which demonstrates Hanafī methodology.
This is a legitimate ikhtilāf; both views are respected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة فصل في القراءة قوله حالة : صَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ (۱) فيصلى سراً. وهذا على سبيل الاستحسان لا على سبيل الوجوب ؛ لأن فيه إحرازاً للفصيلتين، والحق أنه لا مانع من جواز كلّ ما منعوه حالة السكتات ، إذا لم يخـلّ بالاستماع من دون التقييد بوقتِ دون وقت، كما أوضحناه في «السعاية» (٢).
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Recitation. His saying: 'Case: Pray upon him (1) so he prays silently.' And this is on the basis of istihsan, not on the basis of obligation, because in it is attainment of both virtues. And the correct view is that there is no prevention of the permissibility of everything they prohibited during the silent pauses, provided it does not impair listening, without restriction to a specific time, as we explained in al-Si'ayah (2).
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling regarding reciting salutations (salat) upon the Prophet during prayer. The author (commentator) explains that the ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) rather than wujub (obligation). The reason given is that doing so allows one to attain two virtues: the virtue of sending salutations and the virtue of maintaining the prayer's silence at appropriate times. The author asserts the correct position: there is no prohibition against such recitations during the silent pauses (sakatat) as long as it does not disturb the listening to the imam's recitation (if in congregation). There is no restriction to a particular time; any silent pause is acceptable. The author refers to his larger work, al-Si'ayah, for further elaboration.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; in this context, ruling based on preference rather than strict analogy or obligation.
صلاة (salat): Here refers to sending salutations (durood) upon the Prophet, not the ritual prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Reciting salat upon the Prophet during prayer is mustahabb, based on istihsan, and permissible during silent pauses without disturbing listening.

Status of Congregational Prayer: Sunnah Mu'akkadah
Proof and discussion on congregational prayer being sunnah mu'akkadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer and distinguish it from both fard/wajib and mustahabb using the evidence from Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is not fard — it is an emphasized sunnah whose neglect is blameworthy but not sinful.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah tackles a key Hanafi debate: is congregational prayer fard, sunnah mu'akkadah, or merely mustahabb? The commentator presents two opinions within the school and settles on sunnah mu'akkadah. We'll walk through the evidence and understand the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opinions
Read the passage and list the two Hanafi opinions on congregational prayer: sunnah mu'akkadah vs mustahabb.
Note which one is presented as the relied-upon position (mu'tamad).
2
Analyze the primary evidence
Examine the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (man sarrahu an yalqa Allaha ghadan musliman...). Identify the threat and its legal implication.
Pay attention to the phrase 'threat is only attached to abandoning an obligation or an emphasized sunnah'.
3
Understand al-Ayni's interpretation
Al-Ayni argues that the threat (of being a hypocrite) indicates the action is at least sunnah mu'akkadah. Explain why this pushes the ruling above mustahabb but not to fard.
The threat itself is strong but not as categorical as fard; hence the classification as sunnah mu'akkadah.
4
Evaluate the opposing view
The opposing view (mustahabb) uses hadiths with 'afdal' (superior). Explain why the Hanafi school rejects this as weak (shadhdh).
Multiple threat-reports outweigh the single 'afdal' hadith.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
State the mufta bihi (sunnah mu'akkadah) and the practical difference: if sunnah mu'akkadah, leaving without excuse is makruh; if mustahabb, it is not blameworthy.
This shows the importance of resolving intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجماعة سنة مؤكدة فصل في الجماعة (الجماعة سنة مؤكدة) [١]قوله : سنة مؤكدة (۱)؛ هي التي تسمّى بسنة الهدى، وحكمها أنه يثاب فاعلها ويلام تاركها بلا عذر مرخّص، وهذا أحد الأقوال فيه، واستدلوا لذلك بقول ابن مسعود : «من سره أن يلقى الله غداً مسلماً فليحافظ على هؤلاء الصلوات حيث ینادى بهن، فإنّ الله شرع لنبيكم سنن الهدى، وإنهن من سنن الهدى، ولو أنكم صليتم في بيوتكم، كما يُصلّي هذا المتخلّف في بيته لتركتم سنة نبيكم، ولو تركتم سنة نبيكم لضللتم ، ولقد رأيتنا وما يتخلف عنها إلا منافق معلوم النفاق، أخرجه مسلم في «صحيحه». قال العَيْنِي في «البناية»: «دلّ هذا الأثر على أنَّ الجماعة سنة مؤكدة ؛ لأنَّ إلحاق الوعيد إنما يكون بترك الواجب أو بتركِ السنة المؤكدة». انتهى(۳). والقول الثاني : إن الجماعة مستحبّة، ويستدلّ له بأحاديث وردت بلفظ الفضل، كحديث : «صلاة الجماعة أفضل من صلاة الفد بسبع وعشرين درجة»، أخرجه مسلم والبخاري وغيرهما ، لكنه قول شاد مردود ؛ لورود كثير من الأحاديث والوعيد على التارك.
Congregational prayer is an emphasized sunnah. Chapter on Congregation. (Congregational prayer is an emphasized sunnah) [1] His saying: 'emphasized sunnah' (1); it is what is called sunnah al-huda, and its ruling is that the doer is rewarded and the one who abandons it without a permissible excuse is blamed. This is one of the opinions on it. They adduced as evidence the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Whoever wishes to meet Allah tomorrow as a Muslim should guard these prayers where the call to them is made, for Allah has prescribed for your Prophet the sunnan al-huda, and indeed they are from the sunnan al-huda. If you prayed in your houses, as this straggler prays in his house, you would leave the sunnah of your Prophet, and if you leave the sunnah of your Prophet you would go astray. Indeed, we saw that none stays away from it except a hypocrite whose hypocrisy is known.' Narrated by Muslim in his Sahih. Al-Ayni said in al-Binayah: 'This athar indicates that congregational prayer is an emphasized sunnah because threat (of punishment) is only attached to abandoning an obligation or an emphasized sunnah.' End. (3) The second opinion is that it is mustahabb, and they adduce for it hadiths that use the word 'superiority', like the hadith: 'Prayer in congregation is superior to prayer alone by twenty-seven degrees.' Narrated by Muslim, Bukhari, and others. But it is a weak rejected opinion due to the many hadiths and threats against the one who abandons it.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on congregational prayer. The author (commentator) states that the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that congregational prayer (salat al-jama'ah) is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), also called sunnat al-huda. Its legal effect is that the one who performs it earns reward, while the one who neglects it without a valid excuse is blameworthy (gains sin? Actually it says 'yulam' i.e., is condemned, but not necessarily sinful. This is a key Hanafi nuance: sunnah mu'akkadah is not fard, but leaving it is makruh. The author presents two opinions: (1) It is sunnah mu'akkadah, evidenced by the famous report of Ibn Mas'ud, which threatens neglect with hypocrisy. Al-Ayni argues that such a threat is only attached to leaving an obligation or an emphasized sunnah, so it establishes the sunnah mu'akkadah status. (2) It is mustahabb (recommended but not emphasized), supported by hadiths using the word 'afdal' (superior). However, the author dismisses this second view as weak and rejected (shad marbud) because of the multiple hadiths containing threats against the abandoner. Thus the Hanafi position is that jama'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah; its ruling is that the doer is rewarded and the abandoner without excuse is blameworthy (but not sinful).
مستحبة (mustahabbah): Recommended but not emphasized; leaving it is not blameworthy.
شاذ (shadhdh): Weak, rejected opinion; one that contradicts stronger evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position stated in this passage, what is the ruling on congregational prayer?
A) Fard
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Mustahabb
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Congregational prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah in the Hanafi school: rewarded if done, blameworthy if left without excuse.

Ruling of Congregational Prayer: Sunnah Mu'akkadah or Wajib?
Dispute over the legal status of congregational prayer in Hanafi school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on congregational prayer, identify the relied-upon view (sunnah mu'akkadah), and explain the evidence for each position.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah in the Hanafi school, but a strong minority argues it is wajib.

What is the legal status of praying the five daily prayers in congregation? Is it a casual recommendation, a confirmed practice, or an obligation? Within the Hanafi school, there is a spectrum of views. This lesson unpacks the three positions, the evidence for each, and why the majority of Hanafi scholars—and the matn before you—hold that it is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the passage and list the three opinions: (1) sunnah mu'akkadah, (2) mustahabb (rejected as shadhdh), (3) wajib (preferred by some later scholars). Note which is the mufta bihi.
The matn states 'sunnah mu'akkadah' as the default.
2
Examine evidence for sunnah mu'akkadah
Focus on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and al-'Ayni's reasoning. Understand that threat (wa'id) attaches to abandoning a wajib or a sunnah mu'akkadah, not to a mere mustahabb.
The hadith is from Muslim.
3
Understand why mustahabb is rejected
The passage dismisses the mustahabb view as shadhdh because numerous hadiths contain threats against abandonment. A mustahabb act does not carry blame.
These hadiths include threats of Satanic control, sealing of hearts, and the Prophet's intention to burn houses.
4
Evaluate the wajib view
Review the hadiths cited for wajib: burning houses, nullification of prayer for missing the call, etc. Note that these are also used by the wajib proponents, but the majority interpret them as supporting sunnah mu'akkadah.
The wajib view is attributed to many early mashayikh by al-Saruji.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The matn and the commentator affirm sunnah mu'akkadah. Later authoritative texts like al-Hidayah, al-Kanz, and al-Multaqa adopt this. The wajib view, though strong, is not the relied-upon position in the school.
The tarjih authority is the matn itself and later consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجماعة (الجماعة سنة مؤكدة) قوله : سنة مؤكدة (۱) ؛ هي التي تسمّى بسنة الهدى، وحكمها أنه يثاب فاعلها ويلام تاركها بلا عذر مرخّص، وهذا أحد الأقوال فيه، واستدلوا لذلك بقول ابن مسعود : «من سره أن يلقى الله غداً مسلماً فليحافظ على هؤلاء الصلوات حيث ینادى بهن، فإنّ الله شرع لنبيكم سنن الهدى، وإنهن من سنن الهدى، ولو أنكم صليتم في بيوتكم، كما يُصلّي هذا المتخلّف في بيته لتركتم سنة نبيكم، ولو تركتم سنة نبيكم لضللتم ، ولقد رأيتنا وما يتخلف عنها إلا منافق معلوم النفاق، أخرجه مسلم في «صحيحه». قال العَيْنِي في «البناية»: «دلّ هذا الأثر على أنَّ الجماعة سنة مؤكدة ؛ لأنَّ إلحاق الوعيد إنما يكون بترك الواجب أو بتركِ السنة المؤكدة». انتهى. والقول الثاني : إن الجماعة مستحبّة، ويستدلّ له بأحاديث وردت بلفظ الفضل، كحديث : «صلاة الجماعة أفضل من صلاة الفد بسبع وعشرين درجة»، أخرجه مسلم والبخاري وغيرهما ، لكنه قول شاد مردود ؛ لورود كثير من الأحاديث والوعيد على التارك. ومن المعلوم أن تارك المستحب غير ملام فورد ما من ثلاثة في قرية ولا بدو لا تقام فيهم الجماعة إلا استحوذ عليهم الشيطان ) ، أخرجه أحمد وأبو داود والنسائي والحاكم. وورد : «لينتهين أقوام عن ودعهم الجماعات، أو ليختمنَّ الله على قلوبهم» ، أخرجه النسائي وابن ماجه وغيرهما. وورد : «من سمع النداء فلم يأته فلا صلاة له إلا من عذر، قيل: يا رسول الله ، وما العذر ؟ قال : خوف أو مرض) ، أخرجه أبو داود والدارقطني والحاكم وابن ماجة والبَزَّار والعُقيلي وابن عدي وغيرهم بألفاظ متقاربة. وورد : «لقد هممت أن آمر فتقام الصلاة ثم أمر رجلا فيصلي بالناس ، ثم انطلق معهم حزم من الحطب إلى قوم لا يشهدون الصلاة فأحرق عليهم بيوتهم رجال معي بالنار) ، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم ، وفي الباب أخبار كثيرة، موضعها «السعاية». وبهذه الأخبار استند أصحاب القول الثالث ، وهو أنها واجبة، وهو الذي رجحه صاحب «البحر» و«الغُنية» و«البدائع» و «المجتبى»، ونسبه السروجي وغيره إلى عامة مشايخنا.
Chapter on Congregational Prayer (Congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah). His statement: 'confirmed sunnah' (1); it is what is called sunnah of guidance, and its ruling is that its performer is rewarded and its abandoner is blamed without a valid excuse. This is one of the opinions on it. They adduced for that the statement of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Whoever is pleased to meet Allah tomorrow as a Muslim should preserve these prayers where the call is made for them, for Allah has prescribed for your Prophet the sunnahs of guidance, and they are among the sunnahs of guidance. If you prayed in your houses, as this one who stays behind prays in his house, you would abandon the sunnah of your Prophet, and if you abandon the sunnah of your Prophet you would go astray. We have seen that none stays away from it except a hypocrite whose hypocrisy is known.' Recorded by Muslim in his Sahih. Al-'Ayni said in al-Binayah: 'This report indicates that congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah, because threat is only attached to abandoning an obligatory act or abandoning a confirmed sunnah.' End. The second opinion: that congregational prayer is recommended (mustahabb). It is adduced with hadiths that mention the word 'virtue', like the hadith: 'Prayer in congregation is better than prayer alone by twenty-seven degrees', recorded by Muslim, Bukhari and others. But it is a rejected odd opinion, because many hadiths and threats have come against the one who abandons it. And it is known that the abandoner of a recommended act is not blamed. There came (the hadith): 'There are not three in a village or desert where congregational prayer is not established except that Satan overcomes them', recorded by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i and al-Hakim. And it came: 'Let people cease abandoning the congregations, or Allah will seal their hearts', recorded by al-Nasa'i and Ibn Majah and others. And it came: 'Whoever hears the call and does not come, there is no prayer for him except with an excuse.' It was said: O Messenger of Allah, what is an excuse? He said: 'Fear or illness', recorded by Abu Dawud, al-Daraqutni, al-Hakim, Ibn Majah, al-Bazzar, al-'Uqayli, Ibn 'Adi and others with similar wordings. And it came: 'I intended to order the prayer to be established, then order a man to lead the people in prayer, then go with men carrying bundles of wood to people who do not attend the prayer and burn their houses with fire', recorded by Bukhari and Muslim. There are many reports on this topic, their place is al-Si'ayah. And with these reports, the proponents of the third opinion relied, which is that it is obligatory. This is the opinion preferred by the author of al-Bahr, al-Ghunyah, al-Bada'i' and al-Mujtaba, and al-Saruji and others attribute it to the majority of our scholars.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (intra-Hanafi) on the legal status of congregational prayer (salat al-jama'ah). The text begins by stating the matn: 'Congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah).' The commentator clarifies that sunnah mu'akkadah, also called sunnat al-huda, entails reward for performing it and blame for abandoning it without a valid excuse. This is the first of three opinions reported. The proof for this view is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, which includes a threat against abandonment. Al-'Ayni argues that threat only applies to abandoning a wajib or a sunnah mu'akkadah, so the hadith proves it is sunnah mu'akkadah. The second opinion, that it is merely mustahabb (recommended), is deemed shadhdh (odd) and rejected because numerous hadiths contain threats against abandonment, and the abandoner of a mustahabb is not blamed. The third opinion holds that congregational prayer is wajib (obligatory). Its proponents rely on hadiths such as the threat of Satan overcoming the community, sealing of hearts, the nullification of prayer for those who hear the call and don't come without excuse, and the Prophet's intention to burn houses of those who miss the congregation. This view is preferred by several later Hanafi authorities like the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Ghunyah, al-Bada'i', and al-Mujtaba, and is attributed by al-Saruji to the majority of early Hanafi scholars (mashayikhuna). However, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah, as stated in the matn and chosen by the majority of later texts such as al-Hidayah, al-Kanz, al-Multaqa, etc. The passage thus presents three positions, giving evidence for each, with the commentator favoring the first.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregational prayer, specifically the five daily prayers performed in a group behind an imam.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah; a recommended act that the Prophet continuously performed and which is required as a habit. Abandoning it without excuse is blameworthy.
شت (shadhdh): An odd or isolated opinion that contradicts the stronger view; here, the opinion that congregational prayer is merely mustahabb is considered shadhdh and rejected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling of congregational prayer (salat al-jama'ah) for men?
A) It is fard 'ayn (individually obligatory).
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah).
C) It is mustahabb (recommended).
D) It is haram (forbidden).

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position: congregational prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah—rewarded when performed, blamed when abandoned without excuse.

The Hanafi Ruling on Congregational Prayer: Wajib or Sunnah?
Hadith proofs and six opinions on jama'ah's ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer (jama'ah) for men, cite the primary hadith proofs, and explain why the school prefers wujub over sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is wajib for men, supported by severe hadith threats.

The legal ruling of congregational prayer (salat al-jama'ah) is one of the most debated issues across madhhabs. In this passage, the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents strong hadith evidence and then enumerates six different opinions from Hanafi, Shafi'i, Hanbali, and Zahiri schools. The preferred Hanafi position is that jama'ah is wajib (obligatory) for men, a ruling grounded in the threatening language of the narrations. By examining this dispute, you will understand how the Hanafi school derives obligation from zanni proofs and how they reconcile the term 'sunnah mu'akkadah' with practical wujub.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act under discussion
The passage discusses the ruling of salat al-jama'ah (congregational prayer) specifically for the five daily prayers. Determine whether it is wajib, fard, sunnah, or a condition.
Focus on men; women are not addressed here.
2
Extract the hadith proofs
Four hadith are cited. List them and note the common element: severe threats for abandoning jama'ah. Identify the transmitters and the type of proof (ahad hadith).
These hadith are the primary evidence for the third opinion.
3
Map the six opinions
The passage lists six opinions. Create a table: opinion number, ruling, school/sub-school, and any conditions or notes. Pay attention to the Hanafi internal difference.
The third opinion (wajib) is attributed to 'general mashayikh'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi tarjih
The author states that the wajib opinion is preferred by authorities like al-Bahr, al-Ghunya, al-Bada'i', al-Mujtaba, and al-Saruji. Identify why this view is considered mufta bihi.
The threats in the hadith are deemed strong enough to indicate wujub, not just recommendation.
5
Appreciate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if wajib, abandoning without excuse is sinful; if sunnah, no sin but reward is lost. This affects a Muslim's daily practice.
Even within Hanafi school, some called it sunnah mu'akkadah, but the passage argues equivalence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة فصل في الجماعة

وقد ورد: «ما من ثلاثة في قرية ولا بدو لا تقام فيهم الجماعة إلا استحوذ عليهم الشيطان»، أخرجه أحمد وأبو داود والنسائي والحاكم.
وورد: «لينتهين أقوام عن ودعهم الجماعات، أو ليختمنَّ الله على قلوبهم»، أخرجه النسائي وابن ماجه وغيرهما.
وورد: «من سمع النداء فلم يأته فلا صلاة له إلا من عذر، قيل: يا رسول الله، وما العذر؟ قال: خوف أو مرض»، أخرجه أبو داود والدارقطني والحاكم وابن ماجة والبزار والعقيلي وابن عدي وغيرهم بألفاظ متقاربة.
وورد: «لقد هممت أن آمر فتقام الصلاة ثم أمر رجلا فيصلي بالناس، ثم انطلق معي برجال معهم حزم من الحطب إلى قوم لا يشهدون الصلاة فأحرق عليهم بيوتهم بالنار»، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم، وفي الباب أخبار كثيرة، موضعها «السعاية».
وبهذه الأخبار استند أصحاب القول الثالث، وهو أنها واجبة، وهو الذي رجحه صاحب «البحر» و«الغنية» و«البدائع» و«المجتبى»، ونسبه السروجي وغيره إلى عامة مشايخنا.
والقول الرابع: إنها فرض كفاية، وبه قال الطحاوي ومن مشايخنا، وهو أحد قولي أصحاب الشافعي.
والقول الخامس: إنها فرض عين؛ لكنها ليست شرطاً لصحة الصلاة، وهو الصحيح من مذهب أحمد، والقول الآخر لأصحاب الشافعي.
والقول السادس: إنها شرط لصحة الصلاة، وهو أحد قولي أصحاب أحمد، وقول الظاهرية، وليطلب البسط في دلائل هذه المذاهب وغيرها من «السعاية».
[1] قوله: وهو قريب من الواجب؛ هذا الكلام يحتمل ثلاث محامل:
الأول: أن يكون الضمير راجعاً إلى المؤكدة، ويكون الغرض منه تفسير التأكيد، فيكون هذا الكلام موافقاً لكلام مؤلف مجمع الأنهر شرح ملتقى الأبحر: «الجماعة سنة مؤكدة؛ أي قريبة من الواجب»، ولكلام مؤلف «الجواهر المنيفة شرح الدرة المنيفة»: «الجماعة سنة مؤكدة؛ أي قوية تشبه الوجوب». انتهى. ولكلام الزاهدي في «المجتبى شرح مختصر القدوري»: «قلت: الظاهر أنهم أرادوا بالتأكيد الوجوب؛ لاستدلالهم بالأخبار الواردة بالوعيد الشديد». انتهى.
والثاني: أن يكون الضمير راجعاً إلى السنة المؤكدة، ويكون المقصود منه بيان حكم السنة المؤكدة من أنها تساوي الواجب وتقاربه في اللزوم، والعقاب بالترك، كما قال صاحب «البدائع» وغيره: «إن القائل منهم بأنها سنة مؤكدة ليس مخالفاً في الحقيقة، بل في العبارة؛ لأن السنة المؤكدة والواجب سواء، خصوصاً ما كان من شعائر الإسلام». انتهى.
والثالث: أن يكون راجعاً إلى الجماعة، ويكون المقصود به الرد على المصنف له بأن الجماعة أعلى من السنة المؤكدة.
Book of Prayer, Section on Congregation.

And it has been narrated: 'There are no three people in a village or desert where the congregation is not established except that Satan takes control of them.' Narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and al-Hakim.
And it has been narrated: 'People must stop abandoning the congregations, or else Allah will seal their hearts.' Narrated by al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and others.
And it has been narrated: 'Whoever hears the call [to prayer] and does not come, there is no prayer for him except with an excuse.' It was asked, 'O Messenger of Allah, what is the excuse?' He said: 'Fear or illness.' Narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Daraqutni, al-Hakim, Ibn Majah, al-Bazzar, al-Uqayli, Ibn Adi, and others with similar wordings.
And it has been narrated: 'I was about to order the iqamah for prayer, then order a man to lead the people, then go with men carrying bundles of firewood to people who do not attend the prayer and burn their houses with fire.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. There are many other narrations on this topic, their place is in [the book] al-Si'ayah.
And based on these narrations, the proponents of the third opinion relied, which is that it is obligatory (wajib), and this opinion was preferred by the author of al-Bahr, al-Ghunya, al-Bada'i', and al-Mujtaba, and al-Saruji and others attributed it to the generality of our mashayikh.
The fourth opinion: It is a collective obligation (fard kifayah), and this was held by al-Tahawi and some of our mashayikh, and it is one of the two opinions of the Shafi'i school.
The fifth opinion: It is an individual obligation (fard 'ayn), but it is not a condition for the validity of the prayer, and this is the correct view in the Hanbali school, and the other opinion of the Shafi'i school.
The sixth opinion: It is a condition for the validity of the prayer, and this is one of the two opinions of the Hanbali school, and the view of the Zahiri school. Let one seek the elaboration on the proofs of these schools and others from [the book] al-Si'ayah.
[1] His statement: 'It is near wajib'; this phrase admits of three interpretations:
First: That the pronoun refers to the mu'akkadah (emphasized [sunnah]), and the purpose is to explain the emphasis, so this statement agrees with the statement of the author of Majma' al-Anhur Sharh Multaqa al-Abhar: 'The congregation is an emphasized sunnah, i.e., near wajib.' And with the statement of the author of al-Jawahir al-Munifah Sharh al-Durrah al-Munifah: 'The congregation is an emphasized sunnah, i.e., strong, resembling obligation.' And with the statement of al-Zahidi in al-Mujtaba Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri: 'I say: It is apparent that they meant by emphasis obligation, because of their inference with the narrations containing severe threat.'
Second: That the pronoun refers to the emphasized sunnah, and the intended meaning is to explain the ruling of the emphasized sunnah, that it equals wajib and approximates it in necessity and punishment for abandonment, as the author of al-Bada'i' and others said: 'He who among them says it is an emphasized sunnah is not actually in disagreement, but in wording, because the emphasized sunnah and wajib are equal, especially what is among the symbols of Islam.'
Third: That it refers to the congregation, and the intended meaning is to refute the author (of the matn) that the congregation is higher than the emphasized sunnah.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the legal ruling of congregational prayer (salat al-jama'ah) in the Hanafi school, presenting multiple hadith proofs and then enumerating six scholarly opinions from various schools. The author first cites four hadith that emphasize the importance and obligation of attending the congregational prayer, including threats of Satanic control, sealing of hearts, invalidity of prayer without excuse, and the threat of burning houses. These proofs are adduced by proponents of the third opinion, which holds that congregational prayer is wajib (obligatory). This is the preferred view according to many major Hanafi scholars (e.g., Sahib al-Bahr, al-Ghunya, al-Bada'i', al-Mujtaba), and al-Saruji attributes it to the generality of Hanafi mashayikh. Then the text lists three other opinions: the fourth (fard kifayah, held by al-Tahawi and some Hanafis, and one Shafi'i view); the fifth (fard 'ayn but not a condition for validity, correct in Hanbali school and the other Shafi'i view); and the sixth (condition for validity, one Hanbali view and Zahiri view). The passage then comments on the phrase 'wa huwa qarib min al-wajib' (it is near wajib) from the matn. Three interpretations are given: firstly, that the pronoun refers to the emphasized sunnah, explaining that emphasis brings it close to obligation; secondly, that the emphasized sunnah equals wajib in necessity and punishment for abandonment; thirdly, that the pronoun refers to the congregation itself, replying to the matn author that the congregation is higher than an emphasized sunnah. Overall, the passage establishes that the relied-upon Hanafi position is that congregational prayer is wajib, though some express it as emphasized sunnah, which practically amounts to the same.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): The congregational prayer performed in a group, specifically the five daily prayers in congregation.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah, which in this context is nearly equivalent to wajib in terms of necessity and punishment for abandonment.
واجب (wajib): Obligatory; an action whose omission is sinful without valid excuse. It is established by a zanni (probable) proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which opinion on congregational prayer is preferred by the majority of Hanafi scholars (mashayikh)?
A) It is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah).
B) It is obligatory (wajib).
C) It is a collective obligation (fard kifayah).
D) It is a condition for the validity of prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules congregational prayer for men as wajib (obligatory), based on strong hadith threats; the term 'sunnah mu'akkadah' is considered equivalent in practice.

Salah — Prayer

Understanding 'Near Wajib': Three Interpretations of the Status of Jama'ah
Commentary on the phrase 'qarib min al-wajib' with three interpretations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three interpretations of 'qarib min al-wajib' given in the passage and explain how they reconcile the term 'sunnah mu'akkadah' with the practical obligation of congregational prayer.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, 'sunnah mu'akkadah' for jama'ah is practically equivalent to wajib.

The phrase 'wa huwa qarib min al-wajib' (it is near wajib) appears in the matn to describe the status of congregational prayer. The commentator provides three possible interpretations of this phrase, each shedding light on the relationship between 'sunnah mu'akkadah' and 'wajib'. This lesson unpacks those interpretations, showing how Hanafi scholars bridge the apparent gap between those who call jama'ah an emphasized sunnah and those who call it obligatory. By the end, you will understand that the difference is often only verbal, not substantive.

Guided Path
1
Locate the phrase and the pronoun
The commentator analyzes the phrase 'wa huwa qarib min al-wajib' from the matn. Identify the three possible referents for the pronoun 'huwa': the emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), the congregation (jama'ah), or the act of emphasizing.
The pronoun ambiguity is the key to the different interpretations.
2
First interpretation: explaining emphasis
The first interpretation takes the pronoun as referring to the 'emphasized sunnah' itself. The phrase clarifies that 'emphasis' here means it is close to wajib in strength. This aligns with statements from Majma' al-Anhur and al-Jawahir al-Munifah.
This interpretation treats 'sunnah mu'akkadah' as a category that can be near wajib.
3
Second interpretation: equality in effect
The second interpretation takes the pronoun as referring to the 'emphasized sunnah' as a category. The phrase then means that an emphasized sunnah is equivalent to wajib in terms of necessity and punishment for abandonment. This is supported by al-Bada'i' and others.
This view argues that the ruling (hukm) of emphasized sunnah and wajib is the same, especially for symbols of Islam.
4
Third interpretation: the congregation is above sunnah
The third interpretation takes the pronoun as referring to the congregation itself. The phrase then means that congregational prayer is even higher than an emphasized sunnah—i.e., it is wajib. This is a direct refutation of calling it merely sunnah.
This interpretation resolves the dispute by asserting that jama'ah is not merely sunnah, but wajib.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة فصل في الجماعة

وقد ورد: «ما من ثلاثة في قرية ولا بدو لا تقام فيهم الجماعة إلا استحوذ عليهم الشيطان»، أخرجه أحمد وأبو داود والنسائي والحاكم.
وورد: «لينتهين أقوام عن ودعهم الجماعات، أو ليختمنَّ الله على قلوبهم»، أخرجه النسائي وابن ماجه وغيرهما.
وورد: «من سمع النداء فلم يأته فلا صلاة له إلا من عذر، قيل: يا رسول الله، وما العذر؟ قال: خوف أو مرض»، أخرجه أبو داود والدارقطني والحاكم وابن ماجة والبزار والعقيلي وابن عدي وغيرهم بألفاظ متقاربة.
وورد: «لقد هممت أن آمر فتقام الصلاة ثم أمر رجلا فيصلي بالناس، ثم انطلق معي برجال معهم حزم من الحطب إلى قوم لا يشهدون الصلاة فأحرق عليهم بيوتهم بالنار»، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم، وفي الباب أخبار كثيرة، موضعها «السعاية».
وبهذه الأخبار استند أصحاب القول الثالث، وهو أنها واجبة، وهو الذي رجحه صاحب «البحر» و«الغنية» و«البدائع» و«المجتبى»، ونسبه السروجي وغيره إلى عامة مشايخنا.
والقول الرابع: إنها فرض كفاية، وبه قال الطحاوي ومن مشايخنا، وهو أحد قولي أصحاب الشافعي.
والقول الخامس: إنها فرض عين؛ لكنها ليست شرطاً لصحة الصلاة، وهو الصحيح من مذهب أحمد، والقول الآخر لأصحاب الشافعي.

Six Opinions on Congregational Prayer and the Meaning of 'Close to Wajib'
Lists six opinions and interprets a key phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six scholarly opinions on the ruling of congregational prayer and explain the three interpretations of the phrase 'close to wajib' in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school considers congregational prayer as sunnah mu'akkadah, so heavily emphasized it is described as 'close to wajib'.

The ruling of congregational prayer has been a subject of scholarly debate. While the Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah mu'akkadah, other schools assign it higher levels of obligation, such as fard kifayah or fard 'ayn. This lesson presents these six opinions and then unpacks the phrase 'close to wajib' (قريب من الواجب) — a key descriptor in the Hanafi tradition that reveals the intense recommendation behind this act.

Guided Path
1
List the six opinions
Identify all six rulings mentioned in the passage, from the initial sunnah mu'akkadah to the sixth opinion that it is a condition for validity.
The first opinion (sunnah mu'akkadah) is implicit from earlier context.
2
Locate the Hanafi position
Show that the primary Hanafi view is sunnah mu'akkadah, and note that a minority Hanafi (al-Tahawi) said fard kifayah.
The phrase 'close to wajib' is attached to this position.
3
Analyze the three interpretations of 'close to wajib'
Break down each interpretation: pronoun referring to mu'akkadah, to sunnah mu'akkadah, or to jama'ah itself.
Each interpretation shifts the meaning slightly.
4
Evaluate the implications
Understand how these interpretations affect the perceived obligation and punishment for leaving jama'ah.
The third interpretation sees jama'ah as higher than sunnah mu'akkadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي قريب من الواجب
[١]
والقول الرابع : إنّها فرض كفاية، وبه قال الطحاوي من مشايخنا، وهو أحد قولي أصحاب الشافعي .
والقول الخامس : إنها فرض عين ؛ لكنها ليست شرطاً لصحة الصلاة، وهو الصحيح من مذهب أحمد، والقول الآخر لأصحاب الشافعي والقول السادس : إنّها شرط لصحة الصلاة، وهو أحد قولي أصحاب أحمد، وقول الظاهرية، وليطلب البسط في دلائل هذه المذاهب وغيرها من «السعاية».
[1] قوله : وهو قريب من الواجب ؛ هذا الكلام يحتمل ثلاث محامل : الأول : أن يكون الضمير راجعاً إلى المؤكدة، ويكون الغرض منه تفسير التأكيد، فيكون هذا الكلام موافقاً لكلام مؤلّف مجمع الأنهر شرح ملتقى الأبحر: «الجماعة سنة مؤكدة ؛ أي قريبة من الواجب»، ولكلام مؤلّف «الجواهر المنيفة شرح الدرة المنيفة»: «الجماعة سنة مؤكدة ؛ أي قوية تشبه الوجوب». انتهى. ولكلام الزاهدي في «المجتبى شرح مختصر القدوري»: «قلت : الظاهر أنهم أرادوا بالتأكيد الوجوب ؛ لاستدلالهم بالأخبار الواردة بالوعيد الشديد». انتهى.
والثاني : أن يكون الضمير راجعاً إلى السنة المؤكدة، ويكون المقصود منه بيان حكم السنة المؤكدة من أنها تساوي الواجب وتقاربه في اللزوم، والعقاب بالترك، كما قال صاحب «البدائع» وغيره : «إنّ القائل منهم بأنها سنة مؤكدة ليس مخالفاً في الحقيقة، بل في العبادة ؛ لأنَّ السنة المؤكدة والواجب سواء، خصوصاً ما كان من شعائر الإسلام». انتهى.
والثالث : أن يكون راجعاً إلى الجماعة، ويكون المقصود به الردّ على المصنف له بأنّ الجماعة أعلى من السنة المؤكدة.
وعلى كل تقدير فتذكير الضمير بتأويل المذكور، وإلا فالظاهر التأنيث.
And it is close to wajib. [1] The fourth opinion: It is fard kifayah, and that is the view of al-Tahawi among our scholars, and it is one of the two opinions of the Shafi'is. The fifth opinion: It is fard 'ayn but not a condition for the validity of prayer, and that is the sound view of Ahmad, and the other opinion of the Shafi'is. The sixth opinion: It is a condition for the validity of prayer, and that is one of the two opinions of Ahmad, and the view of the Zahiris. Let the detailed evidence for these and other schools be sought from al-Si'ayah. [1] His saying: 'and it is close to wajib': This statement may bear three interpretations. First: The pronoun refers to mu'akkadah, and the purpose is to explain ta'kid, so this statement agrees with the author of Majma' al-Anhur: 'Jama'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah, i.e., close to wajib' and with the author of al-Jawahir al-Munifah: 'Jama'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah, i.e., strong, resembling wujub.' And with the statement of al-Zahidi in al-Mujtaba: 'I say: Apparently they meant by ta'kid wujub, because of their istidlal with reports that contain severe warning.' Second: The pronoun refers to sunnah mu'akkadah, and the intent is to explain the ruling of sunnah mu'akkadah that it equals wajib and approximates it in necessity and punishment for leaving, as the author of al-Bada'i' and others said: 'One who says it is sunnah mu'akkadah is not actually in disagreement, but only in wording, because sunnah mu'akkadah and wajib are equal, especially those that are among the symbols of Islam.' Third: The pronoun refers to jama'ah, and the purpose is to refute the author by saying that jama'ah is higher than sunnah mu'akkadah. In any case, the masculine pronoun is used due to the implied masculine noun; otherwise the apparent would be feminine.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
The passage discusses the various scholarly opinions on the ruling of congregational prayer (salat al-jama'ah). It lists six opinions: (1) sunnah mu'akkadah (stated earlier), (2) close to wajib (the phrase under commentary), (3) fard kifayah (al-Tahawi and one Shafi'i view), (4) fard 'ayn but not a condition for validity (Ahmad's sound view and the other Shafi'i view), (5) a condition for validity (one Ahmad view and the Zahiris). The author then explains the phrase 'close to wajib' by giving three possible interpretations: (a) the pronoun refers to 'mu'akkadah' making the meaning that sunnah mu'akkadah is close to wajib; (b) the pronoun refers to 'sunnah mu'akkadah' meaning this category of sunnah is equal to wajib in obligation and punishment for leaving; (c) the pronoun refers to 'jama'ah' itself, meaning that jama'ah is higher than sunnah mu'akkadah. The author notes that the masculine pronoun is used due to an implied masculine word (i.e., al-madhkur or al-amr).

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A recommended act that is strongly emphasized, approximating wajib in importance but not legally obligatory.
واجب (wajib): A legally obligatory act, the omission of which is sinful, but not established by a qat'i proof (as opposed to fard).
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation; if some Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved; if none do, all sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many distinct opinions are mentioned regarding the ruling of congregational prayer?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Six

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds congregational prayer as sunnah mu'akkadah, but the phrase 'close to wajib' emphasizes its special importance; scholars interpret this phrase in three ways to clarify its legal weight.

Priority for Imam: Most Knowledgeable of Sunnah, Then Best Reciter, Then Most Pious
States the criteria for who deserves to lead prayer and provides evidence and discussion of a counterview

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criteria for selecting an imam, explain the evidence from the hadith of Abu Bakr, and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute with Abu Yusuf regarding the priority of knowledge vs. recitation.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, knowledge of the sunnah takes precedence over recitation when choosing an imam.

Choosing the right imam for congregational prayer is not arbitrary. The Hanafi school outlines a clear hierarchy of qualities. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the three preferred traits—knowledge of sunnah, excellence in recitation, and piety—and the evidence for prioritizing knowledge over recitation, including a key dispute with Abu Yusuf. Understanding this ranking helps you apply the sunnah in mosque leadership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its three categories
The passage lists three qualities in order of preference: the most knowledgeable of sunnah (a'lam bi al-sunnah), then the best reciter (aqra'), then the most pious (awra'). Note that the definition of 'knowledgeable' here is specific to prayer rulings, not all fiqh.
2
Locate the primary dalil for preferring a'lam bi al-sunnah
The hadith 'Tell Abu Bakr to lead the people' from Bukhari and Muslim is cited. Even though better reciters like Ubayy ibn Ka'b were present, the Prophet chose Abu Bakr, indicating that knowledge of sunnah outweighs recitation skill.
The phrase 'muru Abu Bakr fa li-yusalli bi al-nas' is the evidence.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the hadith proves the ruling)
The Prophet's command to appoint Abu Bakr despite the existence of better reciters shows that the criterion for imamah is not recitation alone but knowledge of the sunnah. The incident serves as a specific case (takhsis) of the general rule that a better reciter is preferred.
This is a classic case of takhsis al-amm bi al-sunnah.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf, along with other imams, preferred the best reciter based on another hadith: 'Let the people be led by the best reciter among them.' The Hanafi response is that the Abu Bakr incident occurred after that hadith, so it overrides (naskh) or is more specific.
Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir verified this chronological argument.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position and practical outcome
The relied-upon Hanafi position is to prefer the a'lam bi al-sunnah first. In practice, a knowledgeable imam (even if not a top reciter) should lead over a better reciter with less knowledge. Abu Yusuf's view is not adopted for fatwa.
The tarjih authority is Ibn al-Humam; the position is from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأولى بالإمامة الأعلم بالسنة ، ثم الأقرأ ، ثُمَّ الأورع
[١]قوله : الأعلم بالسنّة ؛ أي الأعلم بالأحكام الشرعية المتعلقة بالصلاة، وإن لم يكن له علم بغيرها، كما في «الخلاصة»، وغيرها، وتقديمه على الإقرار حديث: «مروا أبا بكر فليصل بالناس» قاله له في مرض موته ، أخرجه الشيخان وغيرهما، مع أنه كان ثمة من هو أقرأ من أبي بكر كما يدل عليه قوله : «أقرؤكم أبي بن كعب». وفيه خلاف أبي يوسف، فإنه ذهب موافقاً للأئمة الآخرين إلى تقديم الأقرأ لحديث مسلم والبخاري: «يؤم القوم أقرؤهم، فإن كانوا في القراءة سواء فأعلمهم بالسنة ...» الحديث. والجواب من قبلهما أن قصة إمامة أبي بكر له كانت بعد هذا الحديث، فالأخذُ بها أولى، كذا حققه ابنُ الهمام في «فتح القدير». قوله : ثم الأقرأ ؛ أي إن تساووا في العلم فالاحق هو الأقرأ، والمراد به الأحفظ للقرآن أو أحسنهم تلاوة له باعتبار التجويد والترتيل. كذا في «البحر». قوله : ثم الأورع ؛ أي الأكثر اجتناباً للشبهات، والفرق بينه وبين التقوى أنّ الورع اجتناب الشهوات، والتقوى اجتناب المنهيات قاله ابن نجيم وغيره.
The most entitled to lead is the most knowledgeable of the sunnah, then the best reciter, then the most pious. [1] His saying: 'the most knowledgeable of the sunnah' means the most knowledgeable of the legal rulings related to prayer, even if he has no knowledge of other matters, as in al-Khulasa and others. His precedence over the reciter is based on the hadith: 'Tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer' – said by him during his fatal illness, narrated by the two Shaykhs and others, even though there was someone who was a better reciter than Abu Bakr, as indicated by his saying: 'The best reciter among you is Ubayy ibn Ka'b.' In this there is a disagreement with Abu Yusuf, who went, agreeing with the other imams, to prefer the best reciter due to the hadith of Muslim and al-Bukhari: 'The people should be led by the best reciter among them; if they are equal in recitation, then by the most knowledgeable of the sunnah…' The answer from the Hanafis is that the story of Abu Bakr's leading occurred after this hadith, so acting on it is more appropriate. This is what Ibn al-Humam verified in Fath al-Qadir. His saying: 'then the best reciter' means if they are equal in knowledge, then the most entitled is the best reciter, meaning the one who has memorized most of the Qur'an or recites it best with proper tajweed and tartil. Thus in al-Bahr. His saying: 'then the most pious' means the one who avoids ambiguous matters most. The difference between wara' and taqwa is that wara' is abstaining from desires, while taqwa is abstaining from prohibitions. This was said by Ibn Nujaym and others.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
The passage begins by stating that the person most deserving to lead the prayer (imam) is the one most knowledgeable of the sunnah, i.e., the legal rulings pertaining to prayer, even if he is not an expert in other fields. Then, if there are multiple such individuals, the one who is best at reciting the Qur'an (the most memorizer or the one with best tajweed) is preferred. Finally, if they are equal in recitation, then the most pious (wara'), defined as one who avoids matters that could be sinful or ambiguous, is preferred. The commentator explains that the priority of knowledge over recitation is supported by the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered Abu Bakr to lead the prayer during his final illness, even though there were companions like Ubayy ibn Ka'b who were better reciters. Abu Yusuf disagreed, siding with other imams who give priority to the best reciter based on another hadith. The Hanafi response is that the later incident involving Abu Bakr abrogates the earlier general hadith. The term 'wara'' is distinguished from 'taqwa' by saying wara' is avoiding desires while taqwa is avoiding prohibitions.

Key Terms
الأعلم بالسنة (al-a'lam bi al-sunnah): The one with the most knowledge of the legal rulings related to prayer, especially from the sunnah.
الأقرأ (al-aqra'): The one who has memorized the most Qur'an or recites it best with tajweed and tartil.
الأورع (al-awra'): The one who is most cautious in avoiding ambiguous matters (shubuhat) and desires.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is given priority for leading prayer after the most knowledgeable of sunnah?
A) The eldest person
B) The most pious (awra')
C) The best reciter (aqra')
D) The one with the best character

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when choosing an imam for prayer, knowledge of the sunnah (a'lam bi al-sunnah) is the primary criterion, followed by recitation skill, then piety.

Priority of the Most Knowledgeable in Sunnah for Imamate
States the first priority for imamate with proof and response to Abu Yusuf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on imamate priority and evaluate Abu Yusuf's objection using the chronological argument.

Core Idea
Knowledge of prayer rulings precedes recitation skill in choosing an imam.

Who should lead the prayer? The Hanafi school prioritizes the one most knowledgeable in the rulings of prayer (al-a'lam bi al-sunnah) over the best reciter. This lesson analyzes the proof from the Prophet's choice of Abu Bakr and the disagreement of Abu Yusuf, who favored the best reciter. Understanding this dispute clarifies a key principle in Hanafi fiqh of imamate.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school prefers the most knowledgeable in Sunnah (specifically prayer rulings) for imamate over the best reciter. Note that this is the mufta bihi view.
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf, agreeing with other imams, argued for the best reciter based on the hadith 'The most recitative should lead.' Recognize that this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Compare the proofs
The Hanafi proof is the Prophet's order to Abu Bakr to lead during his final illness, despite better reciters like Ubayy ibn Ka'b being present. Abu Yusuf's proof is the general hadith about recitation priority.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The response is chronological: the Abu Bakr incident occurred after the hadith about recitation, so it takes precedence. This resolves the apparent conflict.
Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir verified this.
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
When the less knowledgeable but more recitative person leads, the prayer is valid but makruh according to the majority Hanafi view, while Abu Yusuf considers it acceptable.

Source Text

Thus verified by Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the first priority for imamate. The author states that the most knowledgeable in Sunnah (particularly regarding prayer rulings) is given precedence over the best reciter. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered Abu Bakr to lead the prayer during his final illness, even though there were better reciters like Ubayy ibn Ka'b. Abu Yusuf differs, favoring the best reciter based on the hadith: 'The most recitative should lead...' The response is that the Abu Bakr incident came after that hadith, abrogating or specifying it. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms
الأعلم بالسنة (al-a'lam bi al-sunnah): The one most knowledgeable of the legal rulings specifically related to prayer, regardless of other knowledge.

Second Priority for Imamate: The Best Reciter (Al-Aqra')
Defines the second priority for imamate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the term al-aqra' in the Hanafi imamate priority order and apply it to determine who should lead the prayer when candidates are equal in knowledge.

Core Idea
After equal knowledge, the best reciter leads—whether by memorization or beautiful recitation with tajweed.

In the Hanafi school, selecting an imam follows a specific order. The first priority is the most learned in Sunnah. But when two candidates have equal knowledge, which quality decides? This lesson unpacks the second criterion: excellence in Qur'an recitation. We will examine the precise definition of 'al-aqra'' as given by Imam al-Haskafi and others, understanding that it encompasses both memorization and quality of recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context of imamate priorities
Recall that the Hanafi order for imamate is: (1) most knowledgeable of Sunnah, (2) best reciter, (3) most pious, etc. This passage addresses the second rank.
The condition 'if equal in knowledge' (إن تساووا في العلم) is the trigger for considering recitation.
2
Parse the term 'al-aqra''
Break down the word 'aqra' – it is the superlative form of 'qari' (reciter). The 'al-' is definitive. The text then glosses it: 'al-ahfaz lil-Qur'an' (best memorizer) or 'ahsanuhum tilawatan' (most beautiful reciter).
The conjunction 'أو' (or) indicates two independent valid interpretations.
3
Distinguish the two aspects of recitation excellence
First: memorization (al-hifz) – having more of the Qur'an committed to memory. Second: quality (tajweed and tartil) – reciting with proper pronunciation and measured pace. Both are valid grounds for preference.
Some later Hanafis prioritize memorization, but the classical view treats them as equals.
4
Note the source and authority
The passage cites 'al-Bahr' (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) as its source, a major Hanafi fiqh reference. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.
The definition is short but foundational for determining imamate in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ثم الأقرأ ؛ أي إن تساووا في العلم فالاحق هو الأقرأ، والمراد به الأحفظ للقرآن أو أحسنهم تلاوة له باعتبار التجويد والترتيل. كذا في «البحر»
His statement: then the best reciter; meaning if they are equal in knowledge, the one who follows is the best reciter. What is meant by it is the one who memorizes the Qur'an best or the one who recites it most beautifully considering tajweed and tartil. Thus in al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage defines the second priority for imamate according to the Hanafi school. After knowledge of Sunnah, the next criterion is excellence in recitation. The term 'al-aqra'' refers either to the one with the strongest memorization of the Qur'an or the one who recites with the best tajweed (proper pronunciation) and tartil (measured pace). This definition is taken from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Key Terms
الأقرأ (al-aqra'): The one who is best in Qur'an recitation, either by memorization or by quality of recitation with tajweed and tartil.

The Third Priority: Al-Awra' (The Most Pious)
Defines the third priority and distinguishes wara' from taqwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-wara', distinguish it from taqwa, and explain why it replaced hijrah as the third priority for imamate in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Wara' means avoiding doubtful matters; it replaced hijrah as the third priority for imamate after hijrah ceased.

This lesson explains the third and final priority for selecting an imam: al-awra' (the most pious). You will learn the precise meaning of wara' (scrupulous piety) and how it differs from taqwa (God-consciousness). The text also shows how the fuqaha replaced the early Islamic virtue of hijrah with wara' as a criterion, showing the evolution of legal standards.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The passage defines the third priority: al-awra' (الأورع), meaning the most pious or scrupulous, derived from al-wara' (الورع).
2
State the definition of wara'
Wara' is defined as avoiding doubtful matters (shubuhat) and excessive desires. It is a higher level of piety beyond merely avoiding prohibitions.
The root meaning is to be cautious, to refrain from what is not clearly halal.
3
Distinguish wara' from taqwa
The text explicitly differentiates: wara' is avoiding desires (shahawat) and shubuhat, while taqwa is avoiding prohibitions (muharramat). Taqwa is a basic religious duty; wara' is an extra precaution.
This distinction is attributed to Ibn Nujaym and others.
4
Trace the historical substitution
Originally, after knowledge and recitation, the next priority was hijrah (early emigration). Once Islam spread and hijrah ceased to be a distinguishing factor, the fuqaha replaced it with wara', based on the hadith: 'The emigrant is the one who emigrates from what Allah has forbidden.'
The substitution shows how legal criteria adapt to changing circumstances.
5
Note the evidence from hadith
The hadith from the Sahihayn provides the basis: the true hijrah is not physical relocation but abstaining from sin. Therefore, wara' embodies the spirit of hijrah in a later age.
Al-Ghunya is cited as the source for this reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ثم الأورع ؛ أي الأكثر اجتناباً للشبهات، والفرق بينه وبين التقوى أنّ الورع اجتناب الشهوات، والتقوى اجتناب المنهيات قاله ابن نجيم وغيره، وقد ذكر في حديث الصحيحين: «فإن كانوا في السنة سواء فأقدمهم هجرة)، فوضعوا الورع مكان الهجرة، بعدما كثر الإسلام وانتسخ التفاضلُ بالهجرة، وصار بالورع ؛ لحديث: «المهاجر من هاجر ما نهى الله عنه». كذا في «الغُنية».
His statement: then the most pious (al-awra'); meaning the one who most avoids doubtful matters. The difference between it and taqwa is that wara' is avoiding desires, while taqwa is avoiding prohibitions. This is stated by Ibn Nujaym and others. It has been mentioned in the hadith of the two Sahihs: 'If they are equal in Sunnah, then the one with the earliest hijrah.' So they placed wara' in the place of hijrah, after Islam spread and the distinction by hijrah was abrogated, and it became by wara' due to the hadith: 'The emigrant is the one who emigrates from what Allah has forbidden.' Thus in al-Ghunya.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage explains the third priority for imamate: al-awra' (the most pious). It defines wara' as avoiding doubtful matters (shubuhat) and distinguishes it from taqwa, which is avoiding outright prohibitions. The author notes that originally the priority after knowledge was hijrah (early emigration), but since hijrah is no longer applicable, the fuqaha replaced it with wara', based on the hadith that the true emigrant is one who avoids what Allah has forbidden. This shows how legal principles evolve with changing circumstances.

Key Terms
الورع (al-wara'): Avoiding doubtful matters and excessive desires.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because hijrah is no longer possible
B) Because wara' is a higher level of piety
C) Because the hadith indicates wara' is the true hijrah
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
The third priority for imamate is al-awra' (the most pious), defined as the one who avoids doubtful matters, and this replaced hijrah as a criterion after hijrah ceased to be a distinguishing factor.

Fourth Priority for Imamate: Age and Additional Tie-Breakers
States the fourth priority and lists additional preferred qualities after equality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of preferences for selecting an imam when candidates are equal in the primary criteria.

Core Idea
When choosing an imam, use definite criteria first; only after all are equal consider age, character, and looks, then draw lots.

You already know the top three qualities for an imam: knowledge, recitation, and piety. But what happens when two people are equally qualified? The Hanafi school provides a clear hierarchy: next consider age, then character, then even appearance or lineage, and finally resort to lottery. This lesson walks through that sequence.

Guided Path
1
Recall the primary criteria
First, ensure candidates are equal in the three primary qualities: knowledge (most knowledgeable of rulings), recitation (best reader), and piety (most God-fearing). These are the basis.
2
Apply the fourth criterion: age (al-asann)
If the candidates are equal in the primary three, select the eldest in age. This is based on the hadith: 'If they are equal in hijrah, then the eldest in age.'
Age here means biological age, not time in Islam.
3
If equal in all four, consider additional qualities
When age also does not break the tie, look first at character (ahsanu khuluqan), then at handsome face or noble lineage (asbahuhum wajhan or ansabuhum). These are secondary preferences.
There is ikhtilaf on which of the two (handsome face or lineage) is preferable.
4
Final resort: drawing lots
If all the above criteria are exhausted and still equal, draw lots (iqra'). This is a legitimate and fair method, not a sign of failure.
Drawing lots is permissible when all reasonable distinctions fail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ثم الأسن ؛ لحديث مسلم : «فإن كانوا في الهجرة سواء فأكبرهم سنا»، قال في «الغُنية»: فإن تساووا في الأوصاف الأربعة قدم أحسنهم خلقاً، ثم إن تساووا فقيل: أصبحهم وجهاً ، وقيل : أنسبهم، فإن تساووا أقرع بينهم.

He said in al-Ghunya: If they are equal in the four qualities, then the one with the best character is preferred; then if equal, some say the most handsome face, and some say the most noble lineage; if they are equal, they draw lots among them.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth priority for imamate: age (al-asann), supported by a hadith from Muslim. After the previous three criteria (knowledge, recitation, piety), if candidates are equal, the eldest is chosen. If they are equal in all four, the text from al-Ghunya mentions additional preferences: first, best character; then, according to some, most handsome face; according to others, noblest lineage; if still equal, they draw lots. This shows the comprehensive approach to resolving tie situations in choosing an imam.

Key Terms
الأسن (al-asann): The eldest in age.
