Gradations of Dislike in Leading Prayer
Ruling on imamate with degrees of dislike.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between prohibitively disliked (tahrimi) and lightly disliked (tanzihi) rulings for different categories of imams and apply the Hanafi gradation.

Core Idea
Leading prayer by a sinful or innovative person is prohibitively disliked; by a slave, bedouin, or child of zina it is lightly disliked; for a blind person even lighter.

This passage from the commentary elaborates on the degree of dislike when certain individuals lead prayer. The nuance is critical: not all categories are equal. Understanding the rationale behind each classification helps you apply the principle of choosing the best imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Categories
List the types of persons mentioned: fasiq, mubtadi', slave, bedouin, child of zina, and blind.
These are not all possible categories, but common ones in classical discussion.
2
Classify the Degree of Dislike
For each category, determine whether the dislike is tahrimi (prohibitive) or tanzihi (light). The text explicitly says fasiq and mubtadi' are tahrimi; slave, bedouin, child of zina are tanzihi; blind is even lighter.
Tahrimi is sinful, tanzihi is not.
3
Understand the Rationale
Note the reasoning: for fasiq/mubtadi', the deficiency is in religious character/creed. For slave, bedouin, child of zina, the reason is possible ignorance due to circumstances. For blind, the lighter dislike because blindness does not affect validity of prayer leading.
The rationale is based on predominant ignorance or lack of upbringing, not certainty.
4
Identify the Exceptional Case
Note the warning: if the innovator's belief leads to kufr, following him is absolutely invalid. This is worse than tahrimi.
This is a threshold: once it reaches kufr, the imamate is batil.
5
Apply the Gradation
When choosing an imam, prioritize based on the degree of dislike. Prefer a tanzihi imam over a tahrimi one, and avoid those whose innovation leads to kufr.
The hierarchy: least disliked (blind) < tanzihi < tahrimi < kufr (invalid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : كره ؛ الكراهة في تقديم الفاسق تحريميّة، وكذا المبتدع ؛ فإنّه أشدّ من الفاسق من حيث العمل؛ لأنَّ فسقه اعتقادي، فإن كان اعتقاده البدعي منجـراً إلى الكفر لم يجز الاقتداء به. مطلقاً. والكراهة في تقديم العبد والأعرابي أي البدوي وولد الزنا تنزيهية ؛ لأنها لأمر محتمل غير محقق ولا غالب، وهو الاستدلال ببعض الشروط بناءً على الجهل الغالب في العبد؛ لاشتغاله بخدمة مولاه، وفي الأعرابي لعدم العلم فيه . غالباً؛ لبعده عن أهله، وفي ولد الزنا لعدم من يشفقه ويؤدبه، وفي حق الأعمى الكراهة أخف، فإنّها
His statement: disliked; the dislike in preferring a sinner is prohibitively disliked, and likewise an innovator; for he is worse than a sinner in action because his sin is in creed. If his innovated belief leads to disbelief, it is not permissible to follow him at all. The dislike in preferring a slave and a bedouin (i.e., a desert dweller) and a child of zina is less disliked (tanzihi); because it is for a possible matter not certain nor prevalent, which is the assumption of some conditions based on predominant ignorance in the slave due to his preoccupation with his master's service; in the bedouin due to lack of knowledge in him often because of his distance from his people; in the child of zina due to lack of one who cares for him and disciplines him; and regarding the blind person, the dislike is lighter.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage explains the degree of karahah (dislike) when certain categories of people lead the prayer. For a fasiq (sinner) or mubtadi' (innovator), the karahah is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), and if the innovation leads to kufr, it is absolutely invalid. For a slave, bedouin, or child of zina, the karahah is tanzihi (lightly disliked), based on assumptions of ignorance or lack of upbringing but not certainty. For a blind person, the dislike is even lighter. This gradation shows the nuanced application of the principle of choosing the best imam.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): Prohibitively disliked; close to haram, but not as severe; it is sinful to do so.
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): Lightly disliked; better to avoid but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is leading by a slave considered disliked (tanzihi) rather than tahrimi?
A) Because slavery is a sin
B) Because of the assumption that slaves may be ignorant
C) Because slaves cannot lead prayer
D) Because it is always better to choose a free man

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grades the dislike of imamate based on the imam's religious condition and likelihood of deficiency.

Preference for Imam and Disliked Imamah
Ruling on dislike levels for various imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imamah of a fasiq and a mubtadi', differentiating between makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Leading prayer while sinful in belief incurs prohibitive dislike; mere social status triggers light dislike.

Choosing an imam for prayer involves more than just knowledge. The Hanafi school grades the dislike based on the imam's character and background. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies who is disfavored and how strongly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the order of preference
The text gives a hierarchy: first by seniority in Islam (based on hadith), then by character, then by appearance, then by lineage, and finally by lot-drawing.
2
Understand the criterion of seniority
The hadith is cited: 'If they are equal in emigration, then the oldest among them.' This establishes age as a tiebreaker when all other factors are equal.
3
Distinguish between fasiq/mubtadi' and others
For a fasiq (sinner in action) and a mubtadi' (innovator in belief), the dislike is tahrimi (prohibitive). For a slave, Bedouin, and child of adultery, the dislike is tanzihi (light).
The innovator in belief is considered more severe than a fasiq in action.
4
Recognize the rationale for each category
Tahrimi dislike stems from the imam's sinful state, which is certain. Tanzihi dislike is based on probable ignorance or lack of nurture, not on actual sin.
5
Note the exception for knowledge
If any of these disfavored individuals is more knowledgeable in prayer than others, they may lead without dislike.
Knowledge can override these preferences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Then the oldest; due to the hadith of Muslim: 'If they are equal in emigration, then the oldest among them.' He said in al-Ghunya: If they are equal in the four descriptions, then give precedence to the one with the best character. Then if they are equal, it is said: the most handsome face, and it is said: the most noble lineage. If they are equal, then draw lots among them. As for the innovator in terms of deeds like the pseudo-shaykhs of our time, he is included in the sinful (fasiq). It is possible that by fasiq is meant more general than both, and the specification of the innovator is for emphasis. His statement: disliked (karih); the dislike in giving precedence to the sinful is prohibitive (tahrimiyyah), and similarly the innovator; for he is more severe than the sinful in terms of action; because his sin is in belief. If his heretical belief leads to disbelief, it is not permissible to follow him at all. The dislike in giving precedence to the slave and the Bedouin meaning the nomad and the child of adultery is of the tanzih type; because it is for a matter that is probable, not confirmed nor predominant, and that is the inference from some conditions based on the predominant ignorance of the slave due to his preoccupation with his master's service, and in the Bedouin due to lack of knowledge in him predominantly, because of his distance from his people, and in the child of adultery due to the lack of one who would nurture and discipline him. Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on the text of al-Wiqayah. It discusses the order of preference for who should lead the prayer (imamah). The first preference is for the one who is oldest in Islam, based on a hadith from Muslim. If all qualities are equal, then the one with the best character, then the most handsome face, then the noblest lineage, and finally drawing lots. The text then explains the categories of people whose leadership in prayer is disliked. The innovator in belief (like Rafidah and Khawarij) is considered a fasiq (sinner) in terms of belief, and their imamah is prohibited (tahrimi). For a slave, Bedouin, and child of adultery, the dislike is tanzihi (lightly disliked) because it is based on probable ignorance. For a blind person, the dislike is even lighter. The passage also clarifies that if any of these is more knowledgeable than the others, they may lead without dislike.

Key Terms
مبتدع (mubtadi'): One who holds heretical beliefs or practices innovations in religion.
كراهة تحريمية (karāhat taḥrīmiyya): A dislike that is close to prohibition; such an act is sinful and discouraged.
كراهة تنزيهية (karāhat tanzīhiyya): A dislike that is not sinful but leaving it is preferable.

Women's Congregation and Mosque Attendance: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on women's congregation and mosque attendance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi relied-upon ruling on women praying in congregation by themselves and explain why it is not disliked, as well as distinguish the ruling for young women attending the mosque.

Core Idea
Women's congregation is not disliked; young women face fitnah concerns.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah addresses two interrelated issues: whether women may lead their own congregation, and whether women – especially young ones – should attend the mosque with men. The base text states a general dislike for women's congregation, but the commentator al-Haskafi challenges this, arguing that all justifications are weak and the correct position is no dislike. However, the presence of young women in men's congregations remains disliked to avoid fitnah, supported by hadith encouraging women to pray at home.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Rulings
Separate the passage into its two main rulings: (1) women praying in congregation by themselves, and (2) young women attending the mosque with men.
The commentator treats each with different evidence and conclusions.
2
Examine the Evidence for Women's Congregation
The base text claims dislike, but the commentator rebuts this with the practice of Umm Salamah, A'ishah, and Umm Waraqah leading women in both Tarawih and obligatory prayers.
This is a dalil naqli from the Sunnah.
3
Analyze the Evidence for Women Attending Mosque
For young women, the ruling of dislike is based on the hadith 'The best mosques for women are the depths of their houses' and the general principle of avoiding fitnah.
The commentator distinguishes between young and old women: young women are disliked in all prayers; old women only in Dhuhr and Asr.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi Position
The commentator explicitly states that the relied-upon view for women's congregation is no dislike, because all reasons for dislike are weak. This is the operative ruling according to later Hanafi scholarship.
The earlier view (makruh tanzih) is still recorded but is considered marjuh.

Book of Prayer, Chapter on Congregation. Page 135. Like the congregation of women by themselves, and the imam stands in their middle if they do so. The word 'imam' applies equally to male and female, thus the feminine ending does not enter it. And like the presence of a young woman in every congregation due to the possibility that she may not guard against impurity. This is all if they are not the most knowledgeable of the people; if one of them is more knowledgeable, he prays behind him. Thus in al-Ghunya and others. [11] His statement: 'Like the congregation'; meaning that the congregation of women by themselves is disliked, whether in obligatory or supererogatory prayers, and they reasoned it with the fact that it does not avoid a prohibited act, which is the imam standing in the middle of the row. But its weakness is not hidden; rather, all justifications that led to the dislike are weak, as we verified in Tuhfat al-Nubala'. We authored it on the issue of women's congregation. We stated there that the correct position is no dislike. How not? Umm Salamah and A'ishah led them in Tarawih and in obligatory prayers, as narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah and others, and Umm Waraqah led in the time of the Prophet by his command, as narrated by Abu Dawud. [2] His statement: 'And like the presence of a young woman'; meaning that the presence of a young woman in the men's congregation is disliked at all times, and an old woman at Dhuhr and Asr, to avoid fitnah and the possibility of corruption, especially in such times. Ahmad narrated from Umm Salamah that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The best mosques for women are the depths of their houses.' Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage deals with two related issues: women praying in congregation by themselves, and women attending the mosque with men. The base text states that women's congregation is disliked, similar to other disliked things, but the commentator (author of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah) argues that this dislike is weak and the correct view is that it is not disliked, citing the actions of the Prophet's wives and other women who led congregations. Regarding the presence of young women in the men's congregation, it is disliked at all times due to fitnah, while old women are only disliked at Dhuhr and Asr when there is less crowding. The commentator supports this with hadith encouraging women to pray at home. However, if any woman is the most knowledgeable, she may lead others without dislike.

Key Terms

الشابة (al-shābba): A young woman who is attractive and thus a potential source of fitnah.

Key Takeaway
Women may lead their own congregation without dislike, but young women should avoid attending the mosque with men to prevent fitnah.

Ruling on Women's Congregational Prayer
Ruling on women's congregation with proof from prophetic practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi ruling on women's congregation and evaluate the proof from the practice of the Mothers of the Believers.

Core Idea
Women's congregation is permissible; the Prophet's wives led prayers.

A common assumption is that women praying together in congregation is disliked. However, a deeper look at the evidence reveals a different ruling. In this lesson, we examine the source text from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya which addresses women's congregation, the imam's position, and the proofs from the Sunnah that establish permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses women performing congregational prayer among themselves. Identify what the correct Hanafi position is: permissible (mubah) and not disliked.
The earlier reported view of karahah is being challenged.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi critique
The commentator criticizes the earlier reasoning that considered the imam standing in the middle of the row as a prohibited act. Recognize the weakness of that argument as stated in the text.
The text says 'la yakhfa da'fuhu' (its weakness is not hidden).
3
Examine the dalil
The commentator provides evidence from the practice of Umm Salama, Aisha, and Umm Waraqa. Identify the type of evidence (Sunnah, ahad) and its relevance.
These are actions and approvals from the prophetic era.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand why the later scholars preferred the view of permissibility over the earlier view of dislike. The strength of the prophetic practice outweighs the conjectural reasoning.
The authority of the later fatwa is from 'Tuhfat al-Nubala'.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning women performing congregational prayer among themselves. The author begins by quoting the matn: women praying in congregation with the imam standing in their middle. He then explains that the word 'imam' is gender-neutral. The commentator notes that some earlier scholars considered this disliked, but he refutes this, stating that the correct view is that there is no dislike. He supports this with the practice of Umm Salama and Aisha (who led women in tarawih and obligatory prayers) and Umm Waraqa (who was appointed by the Prophet as an imam for her household). These ahadith are cited as proofs. The commentary also addresses the condition that if the women are not the most knowledgeable, they should follow a more learned person. The overall ruling is permissibility of women's congregation without dislike.

Key Terms
جماعة النساء (jama'at al-nisa'): Women performing congregational prayer among themselves without male participants, with one woman acting as imam.
تحفة النبلاء (Tuhfat al-Nubala'): A work by the commentator on the issue of women's congregation, arguing for its permissibility.

The Hanafi Ruling on Women's Mosque Attendance: From Abu Hanifa to Later Fatwa
Ruling on young and old women attending mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three stages of the Hanafi ruling on women's mosque attendance (Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, later scholars) and identify the operative fatwa today.

Core Idea
Women's mosque attendance evolved from permissible for elderly to absolutely disliked as times changed.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on women attending men's congregational prayer. You will see how the school's position developed from the early imams to the later scholars, and understand the reasoning based on hadith and changing social conditions.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify the ruling for young women (shabba) and elderly women ('ajuz) according to Abu Hanifa as given in the passage.
Young women: disliked in all prayers; elderly: allowed in maghrib, isha, fajr.
2
Identify the Sahibayn disagreement
Note how Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed: they allowed elderly women in all prayers, but maintained the prohibition for young women.
Their view is more permissive for the elderly.
3
Trace the later scholars' stricter view
See that the mutakhkhirin (later scholars) prevented both young and old from attending absolutely, citing widespread corruption.
This became the mufta bihi according to many authorities like al-Kafi, al-Fath, etc.
4
Analyze the dalil and its interpretation
Examine the hadith cited (Umm Salama, Ibn Mas'ud, Muslim) and how they were interpreted to support the prohibition for young women and permission for elderly originally, then reinterpreted later.
The hadith 'when your women ask permission at night' was restricted to elderly.
5
Determine the operative fatwa and thamarah
State the mufta bihi (absolute prevention) and the practical consequence: an elderly woman may not attend zuhr or asr, or any prayer, according to the later fatwa.
This differs from the original Hanafi position and from the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢] قوله : وكحضور الشابة ; يعني يكره حضور الشابة جماعة الرجال في كلِّ وقت، والعجوز في الظهر والعصر تحرُّزاً عن الفتنة واحتمال الفساد، لا سيما في مثل هذا الزمان، وقد روى أحمد عن أم سلمة أن رسول الله الله قال : «خير مساجد النساء قعر بيوتهن. وأخرج البيهقي عن ابن مسعود له قال : «والذي لا إله إلا هو ما صلت امرأة صلاة خيراً لها من صلاة تصليها في بيتها إلا المسجدين، إلا عجوزاً في منقلها» : أي خفها. وفي «صحيح مسلم» مرفوعاً: «إذا استأذنتكم نسائكم بالليل إلى المسجد وأذنوا لهن، وهذا محمول على العجائز ، قاله العيني) [1] والعجوز الظهر والعصر لا الباقية ) أي لا بأس للعجوزات بالخروج في المغرب والعشاء والفجر. (1) هذا قول أبي حنيفة له، وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : تمنع الشابة من حضور الجماعة مطلقاً، وللعجوز حضور الصلاة ،كلها ولكن المتأخرين منعوا حضور الشابات والعجائز في الصلاة مطلقاً، وعليه مشى صاحب «الكنز» (ص (١٤) ، وقال في «الكافي»: والفتوى اليوم على الكراهة في الصلاة مطلقاً كلها ؛ لظهور الفساد ومتى كره حضور المسجد للصلاة فلأن يكره حضور مجالس الوعظ خصوصاً عند هؤلاء الجهال الذي تحلو بحلية العلماء أولى، ذكره فخر الإسلام، وقال صاحب «الفتح» (۱ : ۳۱۷) : المعتمد منع الكل في الكل إلا العجائز المتفانية فيما يظهر لي دون العجائز المتبرجات وذوات الرمق، وقال صاحب التبيين (۱) : ١٤٠): والمختار المنع في الجميع لتغير الزمان، وقال صاحب التنوير) (۱) : (۳۸۰) : ويكره حضورهن الجماعة مطلقاً على المذهب، وقال الشرنبلالي في حاشيته على الدرر ١ (٨٦) : وهو الأولى، وتمامه في (البحر ) (۱) : (۳۸۰) ، و(رد المحتار (۱ : ۳۸۰).
[2] His saying: 'And like the presence of a young woman' means it is disliked for a young woman to be present among the men's congregation at all times, and for an old woman during zuhr and asr, out of caution against fitna and possible corruption, especially in times like these. Ahmad reported from Umm Salama that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The best of women's mosques are the depths of their houses.' Al-Bayhaqi narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that he said: 'There is no god but Allah, a woman has not prayed a prayer more beloved to Allah than a prayer she prays in the darkest part of her house, except the two mosques, except an old woman in her slippers' meaning her khuffs. In Sahih Muslim it is raised: 'When your women ask permission for the night to go to the mosque, permit them.' This is interpreted as referring to old women, said al-Ayni. [1] 'And the old woman in zuhr and asr, not the rest' meaning there is no harm for old women to go out for maghrib, isha, and fajr. (1) This is the saying of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The young woman is prevented from attending congregation absolutely, and the old woman may attend all prayers. But the later scholars prevented young women and old women from prayer absolutely, and upon this the author of al-Kanz proceeded. He said in al-Kafi: The fatwa today is on dislike in all prayers absolutely due to the spread of corruption. And if attending the mosque for prayer is disliked, then attending gatherings of preaching is even more disliked, especially with these ignorant ones who adorn themselves with the garb of scholars, as mentioned by Fakhr al-Islam. The author of al-Fath said: The relied-upon is the prevention of all in all except the faded old women in my view, not the adorned old women or those with vitality. The author of al-Tabyin said: The chosen opinion is prevention of all due to change of time. The author of al-Tanwir said: It is disliked for them to attend congregation absolutely according to the madhhab. Al-Shurunbulali in his hashya on al-Durar said: This is the preferred view. The full discussion is in al-Bahr and Radd al-Muhtar.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage addresses the attendance of women in men's congregational prayer. It begins with a ruling: attendance of a young woman is disliked in all prayers, while an old woman is allowed for maghrib, isha, and fajr but not zuhr and asr. Proofs from hadith are cited: one encouraging women to pray at home, and another allowing them to attend mosques at night, which is restricted to older women. The passage then documents a major intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa's position is as stated; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree, allowing old women all prayers. Later Hanafi scholars (the mutakhkhirin) took a stricter view, preventing both young and old from attending due to widespread corruption, and this became the later fatwa according to many authorities like al-Kafi, al-Fath, al-Tabyin, and al-Durar. The commentary thus shows the evolution of the ruling over time.

Key Terms
الشابة (al-shabba): A young woman who may attract attention or cause fitna.
العجوز (al-'ajuz): An elderly woman past the age of desire.
الفتنة (al-fitna): Moral temptation or social discord arising from intermingling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Permissible only in maghrib, isha, fajr
C) Disliked in all prayers
D) Absolutely prevented

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on women's mosque attendance evolved from a differentiated permission for elderly women to an absolute prevention due to changing social conditions and the principle of avoiding fitna.

Following an Imam with Different Purification
Ruling on validity of following a leader with different purification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a person with wudu following an imam with tayammum, and explain the proof from the practice of Amr ibn al-As.

Core Idea
The follower's prayer is valid even if his purification differs from the imam's, as long as both are legally valid.

This lesson addresses a common question: can a person who has performed wudu with water pray behind an imam who used tayammum? The Hanafi school affirms this, citing the practice of the Companions. We'll examine the ruling and the evidence, even though the full hadith is not preserved in this text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states: 'The one with wudu follows the one with tayammum, and the one who washes follows the one who wipes.' Determine the hukm: valid or invalid?
The ruling is explicit: it is valid (sahih).
2
Understand the hadith proof
The author cites a narration about Amr ibn al-As leading prayer. What does this report establish?
The hadith is cut off, but it is used to show that the Prophet (PBUH) allowed such following.
3
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools, like the Shafi'i, do not permit a person with wudu to follow a mutayammim when both are present. Contrast this with the Hanafi view.
This difference stems from different understandings of the evidence and the principle that tayammum is a full substitute.
4
Apply the ruling
Consider a scenario: you are traveling, perform wudu, but the imam only has tayammum. Is your prayer behind him valid according to Hanafi?
Yes, as long as the imam's tayammum was valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١] قوله : ويقتدي المتوضئ بالمتيمم ; لما روي أنّ عمرو بن العاص له أمّ
[1] His saying: 'The one with wudu follows the one with tayammum' because it is narrated that Amr ibn al-As led...
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a brief proof regarding the validity of a person in a state of wudu following an imam who has performed tayammum, and similarly, a person who washes his feet following an imam who wipes over his khuffs. The author states the rule and then begins a proof by citing an incident involving Amr ibn al-As, but the text breaks off. The ruling itself indicates that the purification methods are considered valid despite the difference—tayammum is a valid purification when water is absent, and wiping over khuffs is a valid substitute for washing feet. Therefore, the follower's prayer is valid even if his taharah is of a different type than the imam's, as long as both are valid in themselves.

Key Terms
المتوضئ (al-mutawaddi'): One who performs wudu with water.
المتيمم (al-mutayammim): One who performs tayammum due to absence of water.
الماسح (al-masih): One who wipes over khuffs (leather socks) instead of washing feet.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates congregation despite differing purification methods, as long as each person's taharah is valid in its own right.

Old Women and Congregational Prayer: An Intra-Hanafi Evolution
Intra-Hanafi dispute with position evolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on old women attending congregational prayer and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Later Hanafi authorities ruled all women's mosque attendance makruh due to societal change.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya on Sharh al-Wiqayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: which prayers may an old woman attend? The ruling evolved from the time of the founding imams to later scholars who considered the spread of corruption. Understanding this evolution helps grasp how fatwa shifts with time (taghayyur al-zaman).

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling of Abu Hanifa
State which prayers old women are allowed to attend according to Abu Hanifa, as given in the matn.
The matn says 'old woman [may attend] Zuhr and Asr, not the rest' – but the commentary clarifies it means Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr.
2
Note the difference of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allowed old women all prayers but prevented young women absolutely. Understand the reasoning behind each view.
3
Trace the later scholars' position
The mutakkhirin (later authorities) prohibited all women from attending mosque due to corruption, making it makruh. Identify the key sources cited (al-Kanz, al-Kafi, al-Fath, etc.).
This shows the principle of fatwa changing with time (taghayyur al-zaman).
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that attendance is makruh for all women in our times, with a slight exception for extremely aged, non-attractive women.
Al-Shurunbulali says this is the 'first' (al-ula) position.
5
Apply to a real scenario
If an old woman asks about attending a non-obligatory prayer at the mosque, what would you answer?
Practice applying the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[١] هذا قول أبي حنيفة له، وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : تمنع الشابة من حضور الجماعة مطلقاً، وللعجوز حضور الصلاة كلها ولكن المتأخرين منعوا حضور الشابات والعجائز في الصلاة مطلقاً، وعليه مشى صاحب «الكنز» (ص ١٤)، وقال في «الكافي»: والفتوى اليوم على الكراهة في الصلاة مطلقاً كلها ؛ لظهور الفساد ومتى كره حضور المسجد للصلاة فلأن يكره حضور مجالس الوعظ خصوصاً عند هؤلاء الجهال الذي تحلو بحلية العلماء أولى، ذكره فخر الإسلام، وقال صاحب «الفتح» (١ : ٣١٧) : المعتمد منع الكل في الكل إلا العجائز المتفانية فيما يظهر لي دون العجائز المتبرجات وذوات الرمق، وقال صاحب التبيين (١ : ١٤٠): والمختار المنع في الجميع لتغير الزمان، وقال صاحب التنوير (١ : ٣٨٠) : ويكره حضورهن الجماعة مطلقاً على المذهب، وقال الشرنبلالي في حاشيته على الدرر ١ (٨٦) : وهو الأولى، وتمامه في (البحر) (١ : ٣٨٠) ، و(رد المحتار (١ : ٣٨٠).
And the old woman [may attend] Zuhr and Asr, not the remaining. (1) Meaning: There is no harm for old women to go out for Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr. [Hadith: 'The best prayer for a woman is a prayer in the darkest part of her house except the two mosques, except an old woman in her slippers.'] i.e., her khuff. And in Sahih Muslim, raised: 'If your women ask permission to go to the mosque at night, give them permission.' (3) And this is interpreted for old women, said al-Ayni. And in al-Kafi: The fatwa today is of dislike (karaha) in all prayers absolutely due to the appearance of corruption. ...
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling for old women attending congregational prayer, then provides commentary expanding on the matn. The matn: 'Old woman [may attend] Zuhr and Asr, not the rest.' The commentator explains that this means there is no harm for old women to go out for Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr, implying that they are allowed for these three prayers. He then cites a hadith that the best prayer for a woman is in her house, with an exception for old women wearing slippers (khuff). Another hadith from Sahih Muslim permits women to go to the mosque at night, which is interpreted for old women. The passage then discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa's position is as stated; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow old women all prayers but prevent young women absolutely; later scholars (mutakkhirin) prevent all women absolutely due to the prevalence of corruption. The commentator notes that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to later authorities is dislike (karaha) for all women to attend, including old women, unless they are genuinely elderly and non-attractive. The practical consequence is that, in our times, women should not attend mosques.

Key Terms
عجوز (ajuz): An old woman past childbearing age, generally non-tempting.
منقل (minqal): A slipper or khuff worn on feet.
كراهة (karāhah): Dislike; a ruling level between permissible and forbidden, often makruh tanzih.

D) Forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on old women's mosque attendance evolved from permission to dislike, reflecting the principle that fatwa can change with time.

Praying Behind a Mutayammim: Validity of Imamate
Proves permissibility of praying behind one with tayammum or one wiping over khuffs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a person with wudu praying behind a mutayammim and explain the proof from the hadith of Amr ibn al-As.

Core Idea
Tayammum is an absolute purification in its context, equal to wudu, so imamate is valid.

A common question in communal prayer is whether a person with a lower apparent purification can lead someone with a higher one. This lesson examines the Hanafi view that a person with wudu may validly pray behind a person who performed tayammum, and the reasoning behind it. We will also explore the intra-Hanafi disagreement and the decisive proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The text states explicitly: a person with wudu may follow (as imam) a mutayammim. Determine the legal category: is this obligatory, recommended, or merely permissible?
The ruling is that such prayer is valid (sahih), not that it is mandatory to seek such an imam.
2
Understand the Reasoning
The author provides two reasons: tayammum is an absolute purification when water is absent, and the substitution is in the earth, not in the act. This means the imam's purification is complete in its own right.
This distinguishes Hanafi thought from views that treat tayammum as a deficient substitute.
3
Locate the Proof
The hadith of Amr ibn al-As is cited: a junub led prayer after tayammum, and the Prophet did not reproach him. This indicates approval.
The hadith is ahad (single transmission), so it is zanni in both thubut and dalala, but sufficient for practice.
4
Note the Intra-Madhhab Ikhtilaf
Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, arguing that tayammum is a necessary purification while wudu is original. The text responds by clarifying that the earth substitutes for water, not tayammum for wudu.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold the majority position; Muhammad's view is marjuh.
5
Evaluate the Thamarah
The practical consequence: in a community where some have tayammum due to water scarcity, they can lead prayer without requiring everyone to have wudu. This facilitates congregational worship.
The same principle applies to wiping over khuffs: one who washes feet may pray behind one who wipes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقتدي : المتوضىء بالمتيمم، والغاسل بالماسح. قوله : ويقتدي المتوضئ بالمتيمم؛ لأنَّ التيمم طهارة مطلقة عند عدم الماء، والخلفية في التراب عندنا، والغاسل بالماسح؛ لأنَّ الخُفَّ مانع من سراية الحدث إلى الرجل، وما على الخُفْ طَهُرَ بالمسح. وعن عمرو بن العاص : احتلمت في ليلة باردة في غزوة ذات السلاسل فأشفقت إن اغتسلت أن أهلك فتيممت ثم صليت بأصحابي الصبح فذكروا للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال : يا عمرو صليت بأصحابك وأنت جنب فأخبرته بالذي منعني من الاغتسال رجاء أني سمعت أن الله يقول : وَلَا تَقْتُلُوا أَنفُسَكُمْ [النساء:٢٩] فضحك رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ولم ينكره. وهذا حجة على محمد حيث لا يجوّزه بناءً على أن التيمم طهارة ضرورية والوضوء أصلية. والجواب عنه: إن التيمم ليس بخلف عن الوضوء، بل التراب خلف عن الماء، وكما أن الوضوء طهارة أصلية مطلقة عند القدرة عليه، كذلك التيمم عند العجز عنه، فهما متساويان.
And a person with wudu may follow (as imam) a person with tayammum, and one who washes his feet may follow one who wipes over his khuffs. His saying: The person with wudu follows the one with tayammum because tayammum is an absolute purification when water is absent, and the substitution is in the earth according to us. And the one who washes follows the one who wipes because the khuff prevents the reaching of hadath to the foot, and what is on the khuff is purified by wiping. And from Amr ibn al-As: I had a wet dream on a cold night in the campaign of Dhat al-Salasil, and I feared if I bathed I would perish, so I performed tayammum and led my companions in the dawn prayer. They mentioned that to the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم, and he said: O Amr, you led your companions while you were junub? So I told him what prevented me from bathing, hoping that I had heard that Allah says: 'And do not kill yourselves' [4:29], and the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم smiled and did not disapprove. And this is a proof against Muhammad, as he does not allow it based on the view that tayammum is a necessary purification while wudu is original. The answer: Tayammum is not a substitute for wudu; rather, the earth is a substitute for water. Just as wudu is an original absolute purification when one is able, similarly tayammum is an absolute purification when one is unable, so they are equal.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that a person with wudu may validly pray behind a person who performed tayammum, and a person who washes his feet may pray behind one who wipes over his khuffs. The commentary provides the reasoning: Tayammum is considered a complete purification in the absence of water, and the khuff prevents the hadath from reaching the foot. It then presents evidence from the hadith of Amr ibn al-As, who led his companions in prayer after performing tayammum due to cold, and the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم did not reprimand him. This hadith is used against the view of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, who does not permit a person with wudu to follow a mutayammim, on the grounds that tayammum is a secondary purification inferior to wudu. The response clarifies that tayammum is not a substitute for wudu; rather, the earth is the substitute for water. Both wudu and tayammum are absolute purifications in their respective circumstances, so they are equal in authority. Thus, the imamate of a mutayammim is valid.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry purification with clean earth as a substitute for water when water is absent or harmful.
الخلفية في التراب (al-khilafiyah fi al-turab): The substitution lies in the earth (i.e., earth replaces water, not tayammum replacing wudu).
الماسح (al-masih): One who wipes over khuffs (leather socks) instead of washing feet in wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the text consider it valid for a person with wudu to pray behind someone with tayammum?
A) Because tayammum is a form of purification that is equal to wudu in its context
B) Because the imam's prayer is always valid regardless
C) Because the follower's wudu compensates for the imam's deficiency
D) Because the Prophet did not forbid it but that is weak

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a person with wudu may pray behind a mutayammim because both forms of purification are absolute in their contexts, and this is supported by the hadith of Amr ibn al-As.

Standing Behind a Sitting Imam: Prophetic Proof Overrides Qiyas
Ruling with proof: standing follower behind sitting imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a standing person praying behind a sitting imam and explain how the Prophetic action overrides the qiyas of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Prophetic action (nass) overrides qiyas: a sitting imam who bows and prostrates may lead standing followers.

This passage tackles a scenario that may arise due to illness: a person too ill to stand but able to bow and prostrate may lead a congregation of healthy people. The Hanafi school permits it based on the explicit practice of the Prophet during his final illness, despite the analogical reasoning of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Determine the exact scenario: a standing follower behind a sitting imam who bows and prostrates.
2
State the Hanafi position
The prayer is sahih (valid) for both the imam and the follower.
This is the mufta bihi view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
3
Locate the dalil
The Prophet ﷺ led prayer while sitting in his final illness with the congregation standing behind him (Bukhari, Muslim).
This is a qat'i (definitive) textual proof.
4
Analyse the ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani held it invalid based on qiyas (imam's deficiency). The Hanafi response uses the nass to override the qiyas.
The explicit text (nass) takes precedence over analogical reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقائم بالقاعد، والمومئ بالمومئ، والمتنفّلُ بالمفترض. قوله : بالقاعد؛ أي الذي يركعُ ويسجد، وأما الذي يومئ فلا يصح اقتداء القائم به. كذا في «البناية». قوله : على فعل الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم، فإنه صلى قاعداً في مرض موته، والقوم قيام أخرجه البخاري ومسلم، وبهذا النص تركنا القياس الذي ذهب إليه محمد من عدم جواز إمامة القاعد للقائم. قوله : والمومئ؛ أي يقتدي الذي يصلي بالإيماء بمثله؛ لاستوائهما وصفاً. قوله : والمتنفّل بالمفترض؛ لأن الإمام أقوى حالاً، وقد ثبت ذلك من بعض الصحابة في عهد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كما في «سنن أبي داود».
And the standing [may follow] the sitting, and the one who gestures [may follow] the one who gestures, and the one performing supererogatory prayer [may follow] the one performing obligatory prayer. His saying: 'by the sitting' means one who bows and prostrates; as for one who only gestures, it is not valid for a standing person to be led by him. This is as in al-Binaya. His saying: 'based on the action of the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم' for he prayed sitting in his illness in which he died, and the people were standing. This is narrated by Bukhari and Muslim, and by this explicit text we leave the qiyas that Muhammad went to regarding the impermissibility of a sitting imam leading a standing person. His saying: 'the one who gestures' means that one praying with gestures is led by his like, because they are equal in description. His saying: 'the one performing supererogatory prayer [may follow] the one performing obligatory prayer' because the imam is stronger in state, and this has been established from some companions in the era of the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم as in Sunan Abi Dawud.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage expands on the matn which states that a standing person may follow a sitting imam, a gesturing person may follow a gesturing imam, and a person performing nafl may follow a person performing fard. The commentator clarifies: the sitting imam must be one who bows and prostrates, not one who gestures due to illness. The proof is from the Prophet's practice (acting as imam while sitting due to illness, with the congregation standing). This action is used as a text to override the analogical reasoning (qiyas) of Muhammad al-Shaybani, who held it invalid for a sitting imam to lead standing followers. The commentator notes that the standing person cannot be led by an imam who gestures (i.e., only gestures due to disability) because they differ in state. For two gesturing persons, they are equal, so leading is valid. For supererogatory behind obligatory, the imam is in a stronger state (obligatory), so it is permissible, and evidence is from the practice of some Sahaba.

Key Terms
مومئ (mu'mi'): One who prays with gestures (by head movement) due to inability to bow and prostrate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The imam must be elderly or ill.
B) The imam must bow and prostrate.
C) The follower must also be sitting.
D) The prayer must be during illness.

Key Takeaway
A standing person may validly follow a sitting imam who bows and prostrates, as established by the Prophet's action, overriding the qiyas of Imam Muhammad.

When a Gesturing Person Leads Another, and Nafl Behind Fard
Ruling with proof for two situations: mu'mi leading mu'mi and mutanaffil leading muftarid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on a gesturing person leading another gesturing person, and a nafl imam leading a fard follower, and explain the reasoning based on equality of description and strength of state.

Core Idea
A gesturing person cannot lead one who bows and prostrates, but may lead another gesturer; a nafl imam may lead a fard follower because the imam's obligation is stronger.

This passage addresses two additional scenarios from the matn. First, a person who can only pray with gestures (due to severe illness) may only lead others who are in the same condition. Second, a person performing a nafl prayer may lead someone performing a fard prayer, because the imam's state is stronger (he is performing an obligatory prayer). These rulings highlight the Hanafi principle of equivalence in capability and strength.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling
A gesturing person (mu'mi) may lead another gesturing person because they are equal in description (inability to bow and prostrate).
This is based on the principle of equivalence in the ability to perform prayer actions.
2
Identify the second ruling
A person performing nafl (supererogatory) prayer may lead a person performing fard (obligatory) prayer because the imam is stronger in state (his prayer is more emphasized).
The reasoning 'li'anna al-imam aqwa halan' indicates a principle of strength.
3
Note the evidence
The practice of some companions (Sahaba) during the Prophet's time, as recorded in Sunan Abi Dawud, supports the second ruling.
No specific proof is cited for the first ruling beyond the general principle.

Rulings on Standing Behind Sitting Imam, Gesturing Behind Gesturing, and Nafilah Behind Fard
Explains permissibility of certain imam-follower configurations with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of the three imam-follower configurations and explain the proof that overrides qiyas in the case of the standing follower behind a sitting imam.

Core Idea
The Prophet's action overrides qiyas: a standing person may validly follow a sitting imam.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya addresses three key issues concerning who may follow whom in congregational prayer. While qiyas might suggest certain configurations are invalid, explicit prophetic action or the equivalence of states provides the basis for permissibility. We will explore each ruling and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three configurations
The matn mentions: (a) standing person behind sitting imam, (b) gesturing person behind gesturing imam, (c) supererogatory performer behind obligatory performer. Recognize each and note the key condition for (a): the imam must bow and prostrate, not merely gesture.
2
Analyze the proof for the first configuration
The main proof is the hadith that the Prophet prayed sitting in his final illness while the companions stood behind him (Bukhari, Muslim). This text overrides the qiyas that Imam Muhammad used to deem it invalid.
The hadith is a fi'l (action) of the Prophet, which in Hanafi usul indicates permissibility unless proven otherwise.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad opposed based on qiyas: comparing it to the case of a mutayammim leading a mutawaddi', where the one with original purification (wudu) should not follow one with substitute (tayammum). The response: tayammum is not a substitute for wudu; rather, soil is a substitute for water, and both purifications are equal in their own contexts. Thus the analogy fails.
This dispute shows the hierarchy of evidence: text (nass) takes precedence over qiyas.
4
Examine the second configuration
A person praying with gestures (due to inability) may follow another such person because they are equal in description. No qiyas issue; straightforward permissibility.
5
Examine the third configuration
A supererogatory prayer (mutanaffil) may follow an obligatory prayer (muftarid) because the imam is in a stronger state (higher obligation). This is established from the practice of some Companions, as reported in Sunan Abi Dawood.
The reverse (obligatory following supererogatory) is not permissible in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة فصل في الجماعة
والقائم بالقاعد، والمومنى بالمومن، والمتنفّلُ بالمفترض
(والقائم بالقاعد) بناء على فعل رسول الله ، والمومى بالمومي، والمتنفل بالمفترض )
[٤] المتوضئين متيمماً، وسمع ذلك النبي ا ل ل ا ل ل ولم ينكره ) ، أخرجه أبو داود، وهو حجة على محمد ، حيث لا يجوّزه بناءً على أنّ التيمم طهارة ضرورية والوضوء أصلية، والتيمم خلف عن الوضوء، فيلزم اقتداء صاحب الأصل وهو أعلى حالاً بصاحب الخلف وهو أدنى حالا منه. والجواب عنه على ما أشار إليه الشارح الله وغيره : إن التيمم ليس بخلف عن الوضوء، بل التراب خلف عن الماء، وكما أنّ الوضوء طهارة أصلية مطلقة عند القدرة عليه، كذلك التيمم عند العجز عنه، فهما متساويان.
[١] قوله : بالقاعد؛ أي الذي يركعُ ويسجد ، وأما الذي يومئ فلا يصح اقتداء القائم به. كذا في «البناية» [٢]قوله : على فعل الرسول ) ، فإنه صلى قاعداً في مرض موته، والقوم قيام أخرجه البخاري ومسلم، وبهذا النص تركنا القياس الذي ذهب إليه محمد الله من عدم جواز إمامة القاعد للقائم. [۳] قوله : والمومئ ؛ أي يقتدي الذي يصلي بالإيماء بمثله ؛ لاستوائهما وصفاً. [٤] قوله : والمتنفّل بالمفترض ؛ لأنَّ الإمام أقوى حالاً، وقد ثبت ذلك من بعض الصحابة في عهد النبوي ي(٤) كما في «سنن أبي داود».
Book of Prayer: Chapter on Congregational Prayer. And the standing person with the sitting person, and the gesturing person with the gesturing person, and the supererogatory performer with the obligatory performer. (The standing with the sitting) based on the action of the Messenger of Allah, and the gesturing with the gesturing, and the supererogatory with the obligatory. ... the two ablution performers [one with water, one with tayammum], and the Prophet heard that and did not deny it. It was reported by Abu Dawood, and it is a proof against Muhammad, for he does not permit it based on [the argument] that tayammum is a necessary purification and wudu is original, and tayammum is a substitute for wudu, so it would entail the follower of the original (higher) following the substitute (lower). The response to him, as indicated by the commentator and others: Tayammum is not a substitute for wudu; rather, soil is a substitute for water, and just as wudu is an original absolute purification when able, so is tayammum when unable; they are equal. [1] His statement: 'with the sitting person' meaning one who bows and prostrates; as for one who gestures, it is not valid for a standing person to follow him. Thus in al-Binayah. [2] His statement: 'based on the action of the Messenger' for he prayed sitting in his final illness while the people stood behind him – reported by Bukhari and Muslim. By this text we abandon the analogy that Muhammad held, of the impermissibility of a sitting imam for standing followers. [3] His statement: 'and the gesturing' means one who prays with gestures follows his like, because they are equal in description. [4] His statement: 'and the supererogatory with the obligatory' because the imam is stronger in state, and this is established from some Companions in the era of the Prophet, as in Sunan Abi Dawood.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of al-Wiqaya regarding congregational prayer. It addresses three situations: (1) a standing person following a sitting imam, (2) a person praying with gestures following a similar gesturing imam, and (3) a supererogatory prayer following an obligatory prayer imam. The main proof for the first is the hadith that the Prophet prayed sitting in his illness while the companions stood behind him. This text overrides the qiyas that Imam Muhammad used to deem it invalid. The second ruling is straightforward: those equal in inability (gesturing) can lead each other. The third ruling is based on the principle that the imam is in a higher state (obligatory) and thus can lead the supererogatory follower. The passage also includes a subsidiary discussion: the permissibility of a mutayammim leading a mutawaddi', citing the hadith of Amr ibn al-As. Imam Muhammad opposed this based on qiyas, but the majority Hanafi position, relying on the hadith and the equality of the two purifications in their contexts, permits it. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as the relied-upon position is against Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
قائم (qā'im): One who prays standing, able to perform the full prayer.
قاعد (qā'id): One who prays sitting, able to bow and prostrate (not merely gesturing).
مومى (mūmī): One who prays with gestures (īmā') due to inability to bow/prostrate.
متنفل (mutanaffil): One performing a supererogatory prayer (nafl).
مفترض (muftarid): One performing an obligatory prayer (fard).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's action in his final illness establishes that a standing person may validly follow a sitting imam, and this text-based ruling overrides analogical reasoning.

Ruling: A Man Cannot Lead a Woman, Boy, or Hermaphrodite in Prayer
States and proves the impermissibility of a man leading certain categories of followers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a man leading a woman, a boy, or a khuntha in prayer and explain the proof from hadith and legal reasoning.

Core Idea
A man cannot follow a woman, a boy, or a khuntha in obligatory prayer because the imam must be an obligated male adult.

This passage from the commentary establishes one of the key rules of Hanafi congregational prayer: the imam must be a male adult of sound mind and obligation. The text provides both textual proof (hadith) and a rational analogy (qiyas) based on the distinction between obligatory and supererogatory prayer. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the conditions of valid imamate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The passage lists three types of followers a man cannot lead: a woman, a boy (who has not reached puberty), and a hermaphrodite (khuntha). Determine the specific prohibition for each.
2
Examine the proof for the woman
The hadith 'لا تؤمن امرأة رجلاً' is cited, though weak. Understand that despite weakness, the ruling is supported by other evidence and consensus among the Salaf.
Weak hadiths can be used when corroborated by other proofs.
3
Analyze the reasoning for the boy
The key distinction: the boy's prayer is supererogatory (nafl) because he is not obligated (the pen is lifted). The follower is performing obligatory prayer (muftarid). A muftarid cannot follow a mutanaffil in fard prayer.
This is a qiyas: the prohibition is derived from the analogy that the follower's act is of a higher status than the imam's act.
4
Extend to the hermaphrodite
For the khuntha, the rationale is uncertainty of the imam's gender. The condition of being male is not established, so the congregation is invalid.
The khuntha can only lead other khuntha where the condition is waived.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا رجل بامرأة، أو صبي، أو خُنثى
[١] قوله : لا رجل بامرأة ؛ أي لا يقتدى رجل بامرأة ؛ لقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «ألا لا تؤمن امرأة رجلاً ، ولا أعرابي مهاجراً» (١) أخرجه ابن ماجة بسند ضعيف. [٢] قوله : أو صبي؛ إطلاقه يشعر بعدم صحة إمامته للرجل والنساء البالغين مطلقاً، وهذا في الفرض متفق عليه بين أئمتنا ووجهه أن الصبي متنقل، فإنّه لم يفرض عليه شيء، ومن خلفه ،مفترض، واقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل غير جائز.
أما الكبرى فسيجيء توجيهها ، وأما الصغرى فيدل عليها حديث : «رفع القلم عن ثلاثة : عن الصبي حتى يبلغ ، وعن النائم حتى يستيقظ ، وعن المجنون حتى يفيق» (٢) ، ذكره البخاري تعليقا، وأخرجه أبو داود والنسائي وابن ماجة والحاكم وابن حبان وأحمد والدارقطني وابن خزيمة وغيرهم.
فإن المراد برفع القلم رفعُ قلم التكليف، نص عليه ابن حبان، ويشهد له قول ابن عباس له : «لا يؤم الغلام حتى يحتلم ) ، وقول ابن مسعود : «لا يؤم الغلام الذي لا تجب عليه الحدود»، رواهما الأثرم في «سننه»، كما ذكره العَيْنِي في «البناية»
No man [should lead] a woman, or a boy, or a hermaphrodite. [1] His statement: 'No man with a woman' meaning a man should not follow a woman; due to the Prophet's saying: 'Indeed, let not a woman lead a man, nor a Bedouin lead a Muhajir.' Reported by Ibn Majah with a weak chain. [2] His statement: 'or a boy' – its generality indicates the invalidity of his imamate for men and adult women absolutely, and this regarding obligatory prayer is agreed upon among our imams. The reason is that the boy is a supererogatory performer, for nothing has been made obligatory upon him, and the one following him is an obligatory performer, and following a supererogatory performer by an obligatory performer is not permissible. As for the major premise, its explanation will come; as for the minor premise, it is indicated by the hadith: 'The pen has been lifted from three: from the boy until he reaches puberty, from the sleeping person until he wakes, and from the insane person until he recovers.' Al-Bukhari mentioned it as a ta'liq, and it was reported by Abu Dawood, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, al-Hakim, Ibn Hibban, Ahmad, al-Daraqutni, Ibn Khuzaymah and others. For what is meant by the lifting of the pen is the lifting of the pen of obligation, as stated by Ibn Hibban. This is supported by the statement of Ibn Abbas: 'The young boy should not lead until he reaches puberty' and the statement of Ibn Mas'ud: 'The young boy upon whom the hudud are not obligatory should not lead.' Both were reported by al-Athram in his Sunan, as mentioned by al-Ayni in al-Binayah.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn stating three categories of people whom a man cannot lead in congregational prayer: a woman, a minor boy, and a hermaphrodite. The proof for the woman is a hadith, though weak, but the ruling is supported by other evidence and consensus among the Salaf. For the boy, the reasoning is that the boy is not obligated to pray (mutanaffil), and the follower is obligated (muftarid); an obligated person cannot follow a non-obligated one in obligatory prayer. The hadith of 'the pen is lifted' establishes that the boy is not under obligation, thus his prayer is supererogatory. The passage also mentions additional supporting statements from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Mas'ud. The authority weight is from the Hanafi madhhab's relied-upon position; the ruling is agreed upon among the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The khuntha (hermaphrodite) is included because its status is ambiguous and it cannot be certain that the imam is a male, which is a condition for the validity of the congregation.

Key Terms
صبي (ṣabī): A male child who has not reached puberty; not legally obligated to perform prayers.
خنثى (khunthā): A hermaphrodite whose gender is ambiguous; cannot lead because it is uncertain if the imam is male.
متنفل (mutanaffil): One performing supererogatory prayer; the boy's prayer is considered nafl because he is not obligated.
مفترض (muftarid): One performing obligatory prayer; the adult follower is in this category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid for a man to follow a boy (who has not reached puberty) in obligatory congregational prayer?
A) Because the boy's prayer is invalid
B) Because the boy's prayer is supererogatory (nafl) and the man's is obligatory
C) Because the boy is not a male
D) Because the boy cannot recite properly

Key Takeaway
A man cannot validly follow a woman, a boy, or a khuntha in obligatory congregational prayer because the imam must be an obligated male adult.

Three Cases Where Imamah is Invalid: Woman, Boy, and Excused Person
Commentary on three invalid imamah cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three cases where a man's prayer behind an imam is invalid and explain the Hanafi proof and principle for each.

Core Idea
A stronger person's prayer cannot be built on a weaker imam's prayer — this invalidates imamah by a woman, a boy, and an excused person.

This passage from a commentary on Al-Wiqayah explains three rulings where imamah (leading prayer) is invalid in the Hanafi school. The key principle is that a person with a stronger legal status (obligated, fully pure) cannot follow an imam with a weaker status (non-obligated, temporarily pure). Understanding these rulings helps you identify valid congregation and the rationale behind the school's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited imams
List the three categories of persons who cannot lead a man in prayer according to this passage: a woman, a boy (who has not reached puberty), and an excused person (ma'dhur, e.g., someone with chronic incontinence).
The hermaphrodite (khuntha) is also mentioned alongside the boy.
2
For each case, identify the legal reason (illah)
Understand the underlying principle: A woman's place is behind men, so she cannot lead; a boy is not obligated (mutanaffil) while the follower is obligated (muftarid); an excused person has temporary, incomplete purity unlike the follower's absolute purity. In each case, the imam is 'weaker' than the follower.
The strong cannot be built upon the weak is the core maxim.
3
Examine the proof (dalil) for each case
For the woman: a weak hadith 'let not a woman lead a man' and the text 'delay them from where Allah delayed them' indicating obligatory delay. For the boy: the hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' proving he is not under obligation, making him mutanaffil. For the excused person: qiyas (analogy) based on weakness of purity.
The commentary notes the hadith for woman is weak, but the ruling is supported by other evidence.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on the boy leading in nawafil
Some Hanafi scholars (Mashayikh Balkh) allowed a boy to lead in supererogatory prayers like tarawih, but the relied-upon position (mukhtar) in al-Hidayah prohibits it in all prayers because the boy's supererogatory is weaker.
The dispute is about whether the prohibition extends to nawafil; the mufta bihi is absolute prohibition.
5
Apply the mufta bihi and identify practical implications
In practice, a man cannot pray behind a woman, a boy, or an excused person in any prayer (fard or nafl). If done, the prayer must be repeated. If the imam is excused, a pure person cannot follow him, but another excused person may.
The ruling applies to all schools within Hanafi, though some local customs may differ; the fatwa position is clear.

A man (cannot be led) by a woman, or a boy, or a hermaphrodite. [1] His statement: 'A man by a woman' means a man should not be led by a woman, due to the Prophet's saying: 'Indeed, let not a woman lead a man, nor a bedouin lead an emigrant' – Ibn Majah narrated it with a weak chain. [2] His statement: 'or a boy' – its generality indicates the invalidity of his imamah for adult men and women absolutely, and this in fard is agreed upon by our imams. The reason is that the boy is a performer of supererogatory (mutanaffil), for nothing obligatory is prescribed upon him, while the one behind him is obligated (muftarid), and following of an obligated person by a supererogatory performer is not permissible. As for the major premise, its justification will come later; as for the minor premise, it is indicated by the hadith: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the boy until he reaches puberty, from the sleeper until he wakes, and from the insane until he recovers' – Bukhari mentioned it in a suspended form, and Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, Hakim, Ibn Hibban, Ahmad, Darqutni, Ibn Khuzaymah and others narrated it. The meaning of 'lifting the pen' is lifting the pen of obligation (taklif), as stated by Ibn Hibban, and supported by the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'Let not the boy lead until he has a wet dream,' and the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Let not the boy lead who is not subject to legal punishments' – Al-Athram narrated both in his Sunan, as mentioned by Al-Ayni in Al-Binayah. ... They prayed in a corner of the mosque, so he called them and they came trembling, and he said: 'What prevented you from praying together?' They said: 'We prayed in our dwellings.' He said: 'Do not do that; when one of you prays in his dwelling then catches the imam and has not prayed, let him pray with him, for it is a supererogatory act for him. So do not do that if you pray in your dwellings, then come to a congregational mosque and pray with them, for it is a supererogatory act for you.' In Sunan Abi Dawud, Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra, al-Mujtaba, Sunan al-Tirmidhi, and he authenticated it. ... Book of Prayer, Chapter on Congregation: 'And a pure person (may not be led) by an excused person.' [2] Because the obligation is to delay them by text. (And a pure person by an excused person) As for in tarawih and all other supererogatory prayers, the scholars of Balkh permitted his (the boy's) imamah in them, and Nasir ibn Yahya adopted that, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And it is mentioned in al-Hidayah: 'The chosen position is that it is not permissible in all prayers; because the supererogatory of a boy is inferior to the supererogatory of an adult, since he is not obligated to make up for it if he invalidates it by consensus, and the strong cannot be built upon the weak.' [1] His statement: 'Because the obligation' – this is the proof for the prohibition of men being led by women. He did not mention the proof for the prohibition of being led by a boy because it is known from what will come about the impermissibility of an obligated person following a supererogatory performer, and that building the strong upon the weak is not permissible. It would have been better to present it before his statement 'or a boy.' [2] His statement: 'by the text' – it is what Abd al-Razzaq narrated in his Musannaf and al-Tabarani in his Mu'jam from Ibn Mas'ud that he said: 'Delay them from where Allah has delayed them.' And the author of al-Hidayah mentioned it as marfu', but the hadith scholars and commentators like al-Ayni, al-Zayla'i, Ibn al-Humam and others did not find it as such. So this text indicates that delaying women is obligatory, so a woman is not fit for advancing and leading. [3] His statement: 'And a pure person by an excused person' – meaning one who is not afflicted with an excuse should not be led by an excused person, who is one afflicted with a chronic hadath like a mustahada, one with urinary incontinence, passing wind continuously, chronic diarrhea, a flowing wound, and the like; because the healthy is stronger in state than the excused, since the purity of the excused is necessary and temporary, while the purity of the healthy is absolute and complete.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on Al-Wiqayah, explaining three rulings where imamah (leading prayer) is invalid. The commentator clarifies: First, a man cannot be led by a woman. The proof is a hadith (though weak) prohibiting a woman leading a man. The rationale is that women are commanded to be behind men in prayer, as supported by the text 'delay them from where Allah has delayed them,' which indicates that delaying women is obligatory, thus they are not fit for imamah. Second, a boy cannot lead an adult in fard prayer. The reason is that the boy is not obligated (he is mutanaffil – he prays only supererogatorily), while the follower is obligated (muftarid). An obligated person cannot follow a non-obligated person, as the strong cannot be built on the weak. The hadith 'The pen is lifted from three' proves the boy is not under taklif (obligation). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding nawafil (supererogatory prayers): some scholars (e.g., from Balkh) allowed a boy to lead in tarawih and other sunan, but the relied-upon position (mukhtar) in Al-Hidayah is that it is impermissible in all prayers because the boy's nafal is weaker. Third, a pure person (tahir) cannot be led by an excused person (ma'dhur, e.g., someone with chronic incontinence). The reason is that the pure person's purity is complete and absolute, while the excused person's purity is temporary and for necessity, so the pure person is stronger and cannot follow the weaker.

Key Terms
متنفل (mutanaffil): One who prays supererogatory (nafl) prayers; not under obligation.
مفترض (muftarid): One who is obligated to perform the prayer (e.g., an adult performing fard).
معذور (ma'dhur): One who has a chronic excuse (like continuous incontinence) that necessitates temporary purity for each prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a boy not lead an adult in fard prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the boy is not yet mature.
B) Because the boy is performing supererogatory (mutanaffil) while the adult is obligated (muftarid), and an obligated person cannot follow a supererogatory performer.
C) Because the boy has not memorized the Quran.
D) Because the boy may make mistakes in the prayer.

Key Takeaway
A man's prayer is invalid if led by a woman, a pre-pubescent boy, or an excused person, because the imam's status is weaker than the follower's.

A Pure Person Should Not Follow a Ma'dhur: The Principle of Bina' al-Qawi 'ala al-Da'if
Commentary on the ruling of a pure person following a ma'dhur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a pure person should not follow a ma'dhur in prayer and explain the legal reasoning (qiyas) based on the principle that the strong cannot be built upon the weak.

Core Idea
The strong cannot follow the weak: a pure person cannot pray behind a ma'dhur.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling: a person with complete purity (tahir) should not pray behind an imam who has a chronic excuse (ma'dhur), such as ongoing incontinence or istihadah. The ruling is derived from the general legal principle that the stronger cannot be built upon the weaker. Through this passage, you will see how the Hanafi school uses qiyas and a core maxim to determine the validity of congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the ruling explicitly: a pure person should not follow a ma'dhur (person with a chronic excuse) in any prayer. Note the hukm level (makruh tahrimi) and its scope (all prayers, including tarawih and other supererogatory prayers).
The commentary mentions an intra-Hanafi difference: some Balkh scholars allowed a boy to lead in tarawih, but the relied-upon position forbids it in all prayers.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
Identify the proof: the principle that 'the strong cannot be built upon the weak' (la yabna al-qawi 'ala al-da'if). This is a qiyas based on the comparative strength of the purification of the tahir versus the ma'dhur.
The proof is not a direct text but a general maxim applied via qiyas jaliy.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the principle applies: The tahir's purification is absolute and complete (mutlaqa kamilah), while the ma'dhur's purification is temporary and concessional (daruriyya mu'aqqata). Thus the tahir is 'stronger' and cannot follow the 'weaker' ma'dhur.
The strength is in the quality of purification, not in the person's piety.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Disagreement)
The commentary records an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about a boy (sabi) leading in tarawih. Scholars of Balkh allowed it, but the author of al-Hidayah chooses the prohibition in all prayers. This reinforces the general rule.
The hijab for women leading men is also cited, but the focus is on the ma'dhur.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that a pure person should not follow a ma'dhur in any prayer. This is based on the principle of bina' al-qawi 'ala al-da'if and is chosen by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.
The authority weight is zahir riwayah, and the ruling is considered makruh tahrimi.

Book of Prayer, Chapter on Congregation: And a pure person (should not follow) one with a chronic excuse. 139 [2] Because the obligation is to delay them by the text (3), (and a pure person with a chronic excuse). As for tarawih and all other supererogatory prayers, the scholars of Balkh permitted his leading in them, and Nasir ibn Yahya adopted it (1) as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And it is mentioned in al-Hidayah: 'The chosen opinion is that it is not permitted in all prayers because the supererogatory prayer of a boy is lesser than that of an adult, since he is not bound to make it up if he invalidates it by consensus, and the strong cannot be built upon the weak (3).' 1] His saying: 'Because the obligation' is a proof for the prohibition of men following women, and he did not mention the proof for prohibition of following a boy because it is known from what will come regarding the prohibition of one performing obligatory prayer following one performing supererogatory prayer, and that building the strong upon the weak is not permissible, and it would have been more appropriate to present it before his saying 'or a boy'. [2] His saying: 'By the text' is what Abd al-Razzaq narrated in his Musannaf and al-Tabarani in his Mu'jam from Ibn Mas'ud that he said: 'Delay them from where Allah has delayed them' (3), and the author of al-Hidayah mentioned it as marfu', but the hadith extractors and commentators like al-Ayni and al-Zayla'i and Ibn al-Humam and others did not find it. So this text indicates that delaying women is obligatory, so a woman is not fit for advancement and leading. [3] His saying: 'And a pure person with a chronic excuse' means that one who does not have a chronic excuse should not follow one who has a chronic excuse, i.e., one afflicted with a continuous impurity like a mustahadah, and one with urinary incontinence, passing wind, loose bowels, a weeping wound, and the like, because the healthy person is stronger in condition than the excused person. The purification of the excused person is temporary and necessary, while the purification of the healthy person is absolute and complete. (1) He is Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi, who took fiqh from Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani from Muhammad (d. 268 AH). See: al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah (3:546,326) and al-Fawa'id (p.363). (2) End from al-Hidayah (1:358). (3) In Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah (3:99), Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq (3:143), and al-Mu'jam al-Kabir, etc. (4) In Nasb al-Rayah (2:36). (5) In al-Dirayah (1:170).

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on the ruling that a pure person (one without a chronic excuse) should not follow an imam who has a chronic excuse (ma'dhur), such as a mustahadah or one with incontinence. The commentary first explains a previous phrase about women leading prayer, providing evidence from a hadith (though disputed in authenticity) that women should be delayed, implying they cannot be imams for men. Then it addresses the ruling on the ma'dhur. The reasoning is based on the principle that the strong cannot be built upon the weak: the healthy person's purification is complete and absolute, while the ma'dhur's purification is temporary and concessional. Therefore, the healthy person cannot follow the ma'dhur. The commentary also mentions an intra-Hanafi difference: some scholars from Balkh allowed a boy to lead in tarawih and other nafil prayers, but the relied-upon position in al-Hidayah forbids it in all prayers because a boy's nafil is weaker—if he invalidates it, he is not required to make it up by consensus—and the strong cannot be built upon the weak.

Key Terms
طاهر (tahir): A person who is pure and free from any chronic excuse (udhr) affecting wudu or ghusl.
معذور (ma'dhur): A person with a chronic excuse such that they cannot maintain purity normally; includes mustahadah, one with incontinence, etc.
بناء القوي على الضعيف (bina' al-qawi 'ala al-da'if): The principle that the stronger (in terms of ability to fulfill conditions/pillars) cannot follow the weaker in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the primary reason a pure person (tahir) should not follow a ma'dhur (person with chronic excuse) in prayer?
A) The ma'dhur's prayer is invalid
B) The pure person's purification is absolute while the ma'dhur's is temporary
C) The hadith explicitly forbids it
D) The ma'dhur cannot recite properly

Key Takeaway
A pure person should not follow a ma'dhur because the strong cannot be built upon the weak; the ruling is makruh tahrimi in all prayers.
